O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have completed this book, my very dear son, which is the end of the knowledge of medicine together with its content, and I have ended it by its explanations and its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I shall complete this book with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is considered foreign in every way, science and knowledge are perishing and being lost, and nothing remains beyond small descriptions in books written by the ancients that have been changed by hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity; intentions are closed off and knowledge is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	 It seems to me that I should bring it to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And I will come together with the forms of the fire irons for cautery, and other tools of the work with the arrangement of the explanation and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters of hands have been found in our time, the art of medicine has become distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who undertakes it should be versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to such an extent that he knows the judgment of limbs, their forms and joints and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of veins and arteries, and the location of their outlets.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	 And for this reason Hippocrates says that a name without work is nothing.
et meismement en l’art de main.	 And especially in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, should take care not to err and not to cut men.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 As I have often seen more than those who engage in this science abandon science and sense through experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	 I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess from a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of her neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 because so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	 And I saw another fool who removed an arrow from an old man, and the arrow was large.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had been called before to treat him, and saw the state of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	 And I saw another fool who took care of our land's duke who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	 and the foolish man, filled with ignorance, set the break above the wound with strong bindings, and did not leave any slack to the wound, and left it in this state.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	 And he commands that he does not dislocate [it] at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And let it remain in such a way that the leg is completely swollen and the feet come to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	 I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come and dislocate his leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 And when I dislocated it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	 But all ways of corruption are already determined in the member, and cannot be healed.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 And the corruption does not cease to pass through the member until the member is entirely destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And another mirror which collapses and thickens an abscess, and then burns it with the wickedness of its power.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For when an abscess is pure of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in a place where one can remove all that has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary that you know that work with hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	 namely, surgery where there is danger in many situations.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And I will show in every part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	 Therefore it is necessary that you protect yourselves so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	 Take your weapons in a pouch, and attack your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	 And leave the incurable diseases to a grave condition.
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 And remove your weapons from that which causes you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	 Galen said in some of his admonitions:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 "Do not take care of evil disease, lest you be called foolish fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	 "The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and against medicine agues, and these chapters are arranged from the head down to the feet;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 "and of the forms of instruments, and of iron for cauterization, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	 "The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and of boils and wounds, and of the extraction of arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 "and these chapters are arranged and of the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	 "The third chapters are about fixing dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 And it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	 I say that the quality of help, and the harm, is the longest and most subtle speech and the secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	 And many wise men spoke about it and agreed with this.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 And they were satisfied with my words, because I am repeating myself.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	 I say that the cautery helps universally in every constitution or matter, whether it is about constitutions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 meaning hot constitution with matter, and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	 In a hot and dry constitution together with matter, some said and declared that the cautery is of great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	 And others say the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 that fire cautery is not good for disease caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	 For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to treat a hot disease with heat or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 and he who said the opposite claimed that fire provides great help for hot and dry diseases that come in men's chests.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you perceive the body of the man and his constitution is with heat, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this saying.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	 And in every way, do not interfere unless the one who has tested it and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and their symptoms and the time span.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 as for other complexions, we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the observers assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, my son, that cautery combined with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and more powerful than cautery from burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not affect any other member unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	 Burning medications come from one member to another by moving away, and they bring diseases of severe healing to the affected member.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	 and occasionally kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The fire for its high temperature and the goodness of its substance does not cause this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	 And I have found this through experiment and by the length of service and study I have put into the art, and it is above the truth in things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	 And because of this, I excuse the length of my speech, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that is revealed about fire, and the quality of the work, how it eliminates diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstration.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	 Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be performed, and chose companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	 And I say that the cautery is useful in all times, because the harm occurring is beneath hidden by the help of the cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And similarly, when the cauterization is necessary for pain that cannot be delayed until a later time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	 Do not think about it ever, dear child, as foolish people do.
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	 for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return.
et il le dient ensi;	 and they say it this way;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 but it is not as they think, because cauterization is not only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries the humors causing pain, and is more effective than medicine due to the speed of its action and the power of its work and its lordship.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	 And sometimes, the disease comes according to the constitution of the patient and the location of the disease and its properties;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	 The superfluidities are accumulated in him through the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered at the site where there is little superfluity and moisture, as with cauteries for pain, and similar things, and that pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	 but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	 And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the end of medicine, and that is so;
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 But they do not believe that cauteries are effective after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauteries are called the end of medicine because when we administer methods of treatment for a disease and they are ineffective, then we apply the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are the rear of medicine, not according to the intentions of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	 The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are softened more than those of iron, and they did not say this except for the quality of gold and the rarity of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	 and said that the heat of the cautery does not cause pustulation, but this is not always true, for I have proven it, and found it to be true in some men.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 and cauteries made of gold are softer than those of iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	 And yet, when you heat instruments of gold, you do not know if it is heated by the color of the gold and may suddenly cool.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	 and if it is overheated;
si font au feu;	 it burns up.
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And thus there is sufficient obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery that we have found suitable for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I order you this chapter on the head down to the feet, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Hot oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is beneficial for coldness and moisture on the brain, and it is used in the case of a disease called "soda," and for various humors that descend from the eyes and ears, and for many dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and indeed for all diseases caused by coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	 The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a medicine dissolving the head three or four times according to the virtues, the age, and the accustomed capacity of the sick person.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 and then place the head of the patient on the bed.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	 Then make him sit crosswise between your hands, and place his hands on a cushion;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	 Afterwards put the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 and where your middle fingers come, if it bleeds then warm the cautery called "olivare", of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	 And place it on its right position marking it with ink, and make in drawing and pulling your hand little by little turning it.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	 Then lower your hand immediately, and bring the joint back if you see the bone is a bit out.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	 and if you don't see it, continue the cautery until you see the bone as I told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	 Afterwards take a piece of silk, put it wet and soft cotton inside, place it on the joint, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	 Afterwards put soft cotton in butter.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 And leave it until the burn is removed.
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	 And the ancients said, when an overwound stays open longer, it drains more.
et por ce si aide mues.	 and for that reason, it helps to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said to one of these that the fire cautery should be allowed to rest so much that a part of the bone is burnt, and then reset the burnt bone part and heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	 And others say that the cautery should be made less frequently on top, and pushed as hard as a weaver's shuttle so that the humors are forced out from the bone, for this reason because the humors flow out when moved.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	 and the wound should be left open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 afterwards it should be healed and soothed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	 These two ways of cauterization seem not to be good in every case, except for some men who have fear.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	 and it seems to me that I should let it move.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	 For the shoulder is dislocated by continuous solutions of nature, as we have observed in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And likewise, when the shoulder of the patient is weak by nature, and the first indication of the cautery is safer and more effective for me, and from this method I operate together with salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	 When chronic pain comes in the head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use ear drops and pills called "cochie", and cleansing of the head with oil and ointments.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 And if the cautery is performed on him as we have said before, it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	 Be careful that the shoulder of the patient is strong in nature and not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Then cauterize beneath that cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	 Then cauterize the corn at each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and do the cautery that is called "vasselz".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	 and it is the place where blisters are put.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	 And align your hand so that you cannot see down to the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	 The patients feel much greater pain in this cauterization than with others, and I will speak more about it later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 And the cauterizations of the corners must be more subtle than those used to cauterize the midline of the head, and this is their form:
dou cautere dou chief	Fire cautery for the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	 When pain suddenly comes in one part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the head is purged by various medicines, and the other treatments that I have said in the section on diseases have been done, but none of it helps.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 Then make cauteries according to two ways, namely with hot medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	 The cautery with hot medicine is to take a pot of hot water, peel off the bark and pour it over the affected area in such a way that you can place the pot under the skin;
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	 And when it [the dislocation] is reset, let it be held tightly and left thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	 Then loosen the bandage and apply garlic oil to the wound, and leave it as it is for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 Then place cotton soaked in butter on it until it heals completely.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After treating the wound with a remedy until it is healed.
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines that I have written about or use a tenth part of those burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 Instruct the patient as follows regarding the iron cautery.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery in the shape as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	 It is called "clo" because the head resembles the shape of a cloak or has a small hump in the middle.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	 Place it [the remedy] on the painful area and hold your hand still while gently shaking it a little until the middle part of the bladder is burnt.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And lift your hand so that the arteries do not burn, which are outside, and let a profuse flow of blood follow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	 Place cotton on it for three days, and put it on top of it.
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then place dampened cotton in butter, and then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 And if you wish to burn out this abscess with the cautery called "cultellare," all at the tip, be careful not to burn the artery in this abscess that is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	 When treating an abscess as previously stated in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries before mentioned do not fit with the medicine or iron, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	 And so, on the joint, draw a line half a finger's length long, and withdraw your hand once, hold it so as not to cut the artery nor reach the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	 And guard the jaw that is paralyzed when one eats, and let the nerves have no sight but the paralysis, and prevent spasms from coming to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if you are cutting with great fear, especially for him who does not know, and who is not experienced and proven.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	 leave the operation in mid-course.
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 But I will tell you how to stop blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 And if you see that this cautery does not help the disease and the patient is suffering, cauterize it near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	 and if you wish to administer the cautery as we have said or the chapter on artery extraction, use a cautery with two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the cold pain in the ears from frostbite
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear is painful from frostbite and it has been treated with dissolving medicines and other cures as we have said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poins", which is shaped like this:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	 After marking the affected ear all around, or both sides where the pain is present, move a little away from the root of the ear after you have marked the spot.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	 and have ten points around each ear.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After healing the joint until it is sound.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	 The wound that must be cured by fire is not outside those that move from inflammation, as we have said in the classification of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 And do not perform cautery on similar cases coming from scabs and from nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	 When treating this kind of torture which mutes the flow of blood from eyes and purges of the head and gargarism, and it is not worth it; therefore, you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	 One in the root of the ear, and the other a little distance from the temple, and the third at the juncture of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	 and place the cautery in the part that opens healthy, and make it cauterize towards the head of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	 and leave the cautery so that half the hair is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	 And it is the shape of the knife: (The knife mentioned here seems to be slightly more delicate and the blade should be a bit thicker.)
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 after treating the wound as I have said before, until it heals.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	 When the apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient does not have a fever, then perform four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	 Two on the two horns of the head, one in the head, and one at the elbow joint, which is called "wrist" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the stomach mouth:
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 and treat them as we have said before.
de litargie	of litharge
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	 For this disease, give the patient great years and round pills for the brain.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	 Lay the patient on his back completely, and place the mustard plaster (sinapi) on the occuput.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	 and this is the method of the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 If you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	 If it is healthy thus, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	 And if it isn't healthy, you should perform three fire cauteries on the head from neck to collarbone, with a space of one finger between each cautery.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	 and treat it as others, and if you see that it is growing worse, and the patient is enduring it, perform a fire cautery in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if necessary, perform another one on the two horns (temples), and treat it until it is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 And let the cautery called "olive" be as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 The head should be cleaned for years and according to what has been said beforehand.
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	 After the head of the sick person, then make a fire cautery on the head and on each horn, and also behind and 3 times on the spine of the neck.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	 and if you need more, and the body is wet and the patient is suffering, and the disease is far away, make 4 cauterizations on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	 and leave it until the most burning part is burned, and wash your hand.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 After healing until the sick person is healthy, and when the cauterization that is called "olive" has healed as we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epilentics should not use the cautery forcefully except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to modify the skull with other treatments as we have said in the division when the patient is grown and endures to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	 And if it is an infant who cannot suffer it, make a gargle and chew soft foods frequently with good meats.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	 After the king's head is in a middle position, and it is treated according to what was said before, and the fire cautery is applied on the head, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if the patient is out and suffering, apply cauteries as I have said to those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, perform one subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy are the superfluidities or corrupt and swollen fluids, then the cautery of such cauteries should be performed on him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the superfluidities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give him something to drink to purify the brain, as it was before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	 After the king's head of the sick person.
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	 Then make a bandage of linen well made, in the shape of a circle, and place it around the head.
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	 And tie the patient crosswise, and hold them firmly on all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	 After this (line), it is worth the use of old goat's milk.
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	 And the heating with fire should be moderated, so that one can place it on it without causing harm.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	 After hollowing out the circle inside the head (skull), let it cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this to the patient once a week with good management, as long as he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 If you wish to perform cauterization, make multiple pricks throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	 This method of cautery greatly strengthens the brain.
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 Then place damp cotton wool in goat's milk and lard on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first with the signs that I have said in the division, then you begin and give the patient something purifying the head, keep it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or take a bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	 After that, instruct him to lean his head backwards, and perform the cautery in the head (skull) and two more cauterizations on each temple where the disease is present or not present in one.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	 And apply the fire cautery to all the veins and arteries that are beneath the chest, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 And protect against bleeding, and if you see too much blood flowing out, stop it with your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	 And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making the incision with caution how to make it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And sometimes, a cautery or instrument is made under the two bones behind [the chest].
dou cors des larmes	tears of the heart
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	 When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to be above the veins, or have passed through the arteries that appear near the head outside;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	 and it is seen that it is cold phlegmatic fluid, then make the cautery that I have said at the beginning of this work descending into the eyes.
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	 I apply a fire cautery to the head, and I apply two fire cauteries on each temple, and I apply one fire cautery where the hair meets the bones.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 And if necessary, cauterize cautiously above the eyebrow at every small cautery spot.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	When the tears of the body are within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	 When you treat according to what we have said in the previous section, but it does not help, then give the patient three cooked eggs to drink.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	 Afterwards, you roast the head and apply an olive oil-based cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	 And make two cauteries called "clavilis" on each eyebrow, a little under the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 And beware of the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then perform cauterization using this cautery that is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 Here is its shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	 And if you wish to perform the fire cautery on two sorcerers as long as they are like sorcerers themselves,
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 and do not let the hand go unless the third part of the paper is burned, as I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which points the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	 Sometimes, the hairs of an egg are converted to feathers and prick oil; and they make fire cautery according to these methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 This is fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	 The fire cautery instructs the patient to let their hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	 When they are born and become even, then put the patient in bed.
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	 Place a figure of the fernleaf on parchment that is as it is the stalk of the myrtle and the beginning of the sign shaved off from the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 then put softened cotton bathed in egg white and musk of parsley on the oil, then heat the fire cautery as shown in this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	 After cauterizing on the figure you have marked many times, so that the corners are burned there.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	 And the signs of the health of the work are that you see the parchment recede and the hairs lift to the end of the oil.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	 Then lay your hand there, and leave it for three days, then put soft cotton in butter until the burn is healed.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	 And if hairs come afterwards and the paper is softened, then repeat the fire cautery on that same spot, just as you did earlier.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if the hairs fall out, then cauterize it until the paper returns to its natural position and becomes even, and do not let the hairs grow oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	 The medical fire-cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	 Then take French soap and live coal, one of each. Grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	 and make it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the form in the shape of a mimosa leaf, and place it over the eyes.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	 and if the patient only holds onto one eye, you must work on both of them.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	 and place a cotton swab moistened with oil underneath an eggshell.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 and the patient's shoulder should be in your hand, and place your thumb showing above the medicine, and press the edge and move all around whenever the patient feels burning from the medicine, as it burns like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done so for a long time, give the medicine at your shoulder.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	 And when the bone is broken, lift the limb upward, and look to see if the piece of bone has been raised as it was raised by the action of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 If it is like that, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	 If it is not like that, then put more medicine on the limb or the medicine has not worked, as long as your efforts are even and your hands placed correctly;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then place cotton soaked in butter on the wound until the burn is healed, then clean the limb with an ointment called "diaphensis" and others until it is healthy;
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if it is necessary for you to be careful about your work, keep far away from the eyes with great care so that no medicine reaches them.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	 And if the bone becomes soft afterwards and the hairs prick in the oil, then start the medicine on that limb which has been made soft by the bone itself, just as you did before;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 After the cure when it is healthy;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 and this is the form of the thorny plant, the nettle.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	 And know that human eyes are diverse in size and shape, according to your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And the right path should not be deviated from one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On treating a fistula with cautery.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you perform cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	 Instruct the patient to put his head on your holy object;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	 and the ministers should grasp the patient's head between their hands in such a manner that it does not move or tilt its head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	 After placing cotton wool soaked in egg white or onion juice on top of the oil;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	 After heating the fire-tong which is this:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	 and positioned at the base of the head in a manner similar to the shape of a quill from a feather, along with the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	 If it appears, it should be pointed from one head to the other, and if it appears, it should also look like a tent.
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 But nevertheless, this which is placed on top serves for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	 After pressing the fistula when it has opened, take out the pus and dry it.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	 And if it is closed, you open it, and draw out the worms.
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	 Then put hot iron cautery on it, and hold your hand on the cautery on the part of the nail below the oil, so that your hand does not move.
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Put the cautery in the oil fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come at the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	 If that does not work, repeat the cauterization again if necessary, and leave it for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	 After placing cotton wool in butter, apply the drying ointment until it is dry, and if after 40 days it is not dry, apply a corrosive medicine while the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 And the king according to what he writes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a way of making a fire cautery which no ancient person spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	 For a fistula (an abnormal passage or cavity between two organs), make an incision and open it up.
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 After putting camphor of the fine form given below in the incision:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	 and they put as much as a half-pint (approx. 946 milliliters) of liquid.
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	 Hold your hand with the camphor firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the liquid does not spill over.
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	 And it is necessary to apply oil to the patient, cotton soaked with egg yolk or walnut oil.
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 The plug is drawn from the fistula, and health comes marvelously through it.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the fire cautery as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then administer oil of roses or bring the fistula to the body heat as is appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cavities in lips called "hairs" and also in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat the cavities as we have described in previous sections and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery scalpel of this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	 And it should be put immediately into those cavities until it reaches the source.
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After curing the wound with lime until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	 When an abscess comes at the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the teeth roots, after it has turned into pus and becomes inflamed and turns into a fistula.
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	 and you treat it as we have said in the previous section, but it does not help at all.
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	 Then it is necessary to use the cautery according to the size of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	 After the bottle or perforation of the fistula, hold your hand until the iron comes to its end, and where it exits.
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and do this once or twice, after treating what we have said in the treatment, until it is healed;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	 if it heals like this, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 and if not, it is necessary to discover the location and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	The movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but it does not help, then put the head of the patient on your lap;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	 After heating the cautery in this way, take a cane and place it on the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	 And put hot fire cautery inside promptly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat approaching the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	 After moving your hand, continue with the cautery as you wish;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 Then fill the patient's mouth with saltwater, and keep it there for an hour and rinse far inside.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the moving tooth is made stationary, the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupting moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	From the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	 When tooth pain comes from coldness or there is coldness and pus, and the medicinal cures are of no value, then it will be necessary to use cautery in two ways:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 And cautery made with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	 The cautery of butter is such that you take butter from a cow, and the tip in an iron or copper spoon.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	 After taking cotton and wrapping it on the tip of a lance, and boiling it in butter, place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it is cooled.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 and perform this often until its properties reach the root of the tooth, and if you see cotton and wool soaked in cold butter, place it on the tooth, and hold the hot iron to it until the heat reaches the tooth's nerve.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	 The fire cautery is such that you take a rod of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough so that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	 After heating the cautery, when its shape comes later, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 Make it often, for the pain will be stopped on that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	 And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in haste for this cautery, and then hold his breath.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	 And make the cautery on the head that you wish, and according to what you are able;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	 and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	 When scrofula is from cold and damp conditions, and is not obedient to digestion by medications, then heat the cautery as described below, and have it two openings for the smoke to escape to the other side of the cautery.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	 And place the hot cautery on the abscess once, wherever it is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess.
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	 And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its size, and leave it so for three days.
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	 And place dampened cotton on it until the arrow is removed;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After healing the wound with ointments and plasters, let it become clean.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The form of the shoulder blade:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	 When moisture prevails over the channel of the intestine, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be purged with soluble medicines.
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 After performing cautery at the root of the throat, be careful not to approach the throat itself, and do not go too deep but only a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	 Afterwards, perform the other fire cautery at the joint of the neck with the spine, and it is the cautery called "clavicle," as we have known its form.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal the limb as we have previously said until it becomes healthy.
de la toust	tooth
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	 When all and scrofula are due to cold moisture, and the patient does not have fever or itch, and the disease is old, perform two cauteries on the scrotum in visible limbs.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	 And perform another cautery between the testicles.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 And let it be the cautery called "clavicle" according to the form that has previously been described.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	 And if you see, perform a cautery by pricking all over the cautery called "points" as its form is described above in the ear disease.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And let the points [of the instruments] be up to thirty, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After treating the limb as previously stated, let the cautery be at three intervals according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because the cauterization is lighter, because you make them in pairs of two.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	 Make sure the patient is lying on his back and on his side [alternately].
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	 then grasp the key that is within the tooth of your left hand [i.e., forceps or extractor].
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 if the jointure is dislocated, then heat the cautery with two nerves [tongs] of this kind [hot iron].
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	 cauterize the key until it pierces the chest and produces a figure with four cauteries.
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	 this is done using the cautery with three nerves, which is why the figures of cauterization are [made up of] several cauteries.
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tendon, this is the shape of the cautery with three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	Sometimes it is sewn up on this one nerve, which is why there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	 After place on the fire cautery, grind with ashes.
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 after the patient has rested, and his limbs are not moved for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 If it is dislocated above [the joint], which happens little, then do cautery on the thick part of the cautery rod, or many cauteries while pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 For the joint is reset, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach there are coldness and much moisture that increase its complexion, and the catarrh multiplies in him, and in the usual methods of treatment he does not benefit; therefore, the patient should be supine on his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	 Then do three cauteries in the area under the spoonful of pus, on all the cautery sticks, and two cauteries outside the two costal areas so that the figure of the cauteries is at three angles, and with such space between one and another that they are not joined together when they emit pus.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 and the cautery points should be deep enough to prick the two parts of the body cavity, and the figure of the cauteries according to this form without deviation.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	 And he who fears this cautery, cauterize by pricking and applying on the stomach at a point according to the quantity that you see fit;
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 Then cauterize the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the healing of the wound is complete, when it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	 When the liver experiences pain due to cold, moisture and great windiness, as it is forced out of its natural composition by excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	 And the patient is cured of what has been said in previous sections, but it does not help him, so the patient must be kept on his bedclothes;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	 Sign the third cautery according to this form, shape and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondriac region, where the ribs of the chest come together;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	 And let there be space between each fire cautery, the thickness of two fingers.
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	 And let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press too hard with your hand on all the cautery.
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	 Burn only the middle part of the curd, and make the patient straight on his feet.
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	 If he cannot stand, let him be lying down, and extend his legs and raise his arms.
et c’est li forme:	 And this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	 If you so desire, you may cauterize these cauteries with a surgeon's knife, if you are skillful and knowledgeable in the art, but be careful not to burn too much because you will scorch the whole body.
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And it should not go down to the boil, because the area is very subtle there, and only the knowledgeable can see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	 When he has an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the fat of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	 if it is in the fat, the patient feels pain not very strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	 And when this treatment ceases, it is necessary that the patient rest on his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 and then press firmly on the side or place where the abscess is, and then heat the iron similar to a coin, which is the shape of the following form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	 Heat the iron until it glows red, and bring it up to the wound until it is completely open;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	 after treatment according to the treatment for boils until it heals.
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 It is not advisable to use this fire cautery method by anyone who has not thoroughly studied the art of medicine, for many times these diseases have been caused by such practices.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Afterwards it can be boldly operated, and yet I think it is better to wait.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	 They said that for cauterization at pleurisy, one should use the roots of Aristolochia, and in this manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	 Take a long root of Aristolochia, the largest one you can find, and it should be dry and as thick and long as your fingers.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	 and wet it in oil, heat it up, and cauterize the cautery between the ribs and the collar, and make small cauteries a little below the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	 and the cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, in a slightly descending direction.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	 And the cautery enters into the worst place, and the other on the stomach, and between the shoulders, and the two at the sides beyond the cautery which is between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 And do not press your hand, instead make it open as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	 And an old man said that no one uses the fire cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And jumps out of the pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear or death of the patient now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	For the mouse cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the divisions of treatment, and it does not help, then they suggested four methods of cautery that are all good.
