et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	 And when you feel it with your hands, you should squeeze it tightly.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	 And when it is due to the vein, it appears clearly apparent.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 It is foolish to cover this abscess and especially when it is under the armpits and near the angles or neck and in many other places, and they are very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	 Therefore the iron cure should be removed, and the one on the head should also be removed, and in the case of an inflamed artery, make an incision above the skin with a long blade.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	 then open the abdomen in one piece and carefully separate the artery from the ligaments, until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	 then insert an awl beneath it and make it penetrate until the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread in two places as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	 Then leave the joint between the two ligaments of an intromissoire until the pus within it breaks open, and the abscess should be broken.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	 then apply the treatment that causes a swelling, as long as the ligament is breaking.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then treat this with liniment until it heals completely.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	 and if the abscess is for the sake of opening a vein, then you must paint your hand with whatever can be obtained from the abscess all over the skin, then insert the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce through, and there should be double thread, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	 then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or a ligament of one part to another between the two shoulders with thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	 And if you doubt that the thread does not go through, push another needle under the abscess at the incision of the first needle and hold the thread in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	 then press the abscess until the excess goes out, then press the pus and leave what is connected.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then give it treatments of tents (bandages) and liniments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of the flesh
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As in arteries and veins, abscesses come to the nerves when they are struck or due to excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	 This happens more often in the shoulder and thumb and in all places where there are joints, and it is the serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it occurs in many different positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	 And when it is strained, the patient feels pain, and it does not go completely through the body but under the flesh.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	 It should be completely silent from all sides and does not go forward or backward, neither underneath nor above, and the one in the joints should not be covered with iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	 In case it contracts.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And if it is on the head or forehead, scrape the skin with the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	 If the abscess is small, take tweezers and hit it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is large, suspend it to the incision and peel it off, then open it and stitch up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Heavy growths hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	 Sometimes happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" because of its resemblance to birds, and it has subtle roots and large heads.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	 and it has small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 and I saw a man who had two bellies that resembled fungi more than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a small root, and were split open, and ran moisture continuously.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	 I weighed them and found one to weigh eighteen ounces, and the other six, and the work in the incision is such that you can see if the patient is moist, and the color of the arrowhead is white and wet and has a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 If the head of the spatula is large and the fire cautery is present with you.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	 For at the cutting often comes too great evacuations of blood, and if it escapes from you, hasten then to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	 and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the iron incision, take well-made thread, tie it as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	 then you hold it tight and do not stop holding the thread of yarn until the head of the arrow feels working.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	 and if the roots are thick, you should fear to treat it yourself by the belly, but you can cover half of it well, then cauterize it so that it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 Then heal the wound, and ensure you do not cover the yellowish substance which is of foul smell and poor sensation with milk-like discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess swollen, and I will come to the treatment for gonorrhea afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boil bursts out
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	 If the boil appears due to cautery of a wound or a fissure in the belly and some of the boils are on it, as happens in other routes, or from blood that leaks from veins or arteries as mentioned before, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 And if it is by the fracture of the sinew and by the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it causes little pain, and has an open wound with various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the intestine, then it is more diverse. When you press it with your fingers, it retracts and then comes back, and in some cases, it becomes hard, and greatly swells at the entrance of the wound, and due to much labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	 And if it is due to blood, the abscess becomes large and hard, and is filled according to a certain quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to windiness, it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you look to see if its appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary that you let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For it has doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	 And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the belly, you should instruct the patient to lean their back, and be extended straight, then hold all around the belly.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	 then command him to press gently between your hands, then go around the place you have signed with all the spatula, then spread half of the abscess above with a large spoon.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	 then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the patient be in a relaxed state.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	 then open half of the extended abscess with the thread, and insert your index finger, and try to find the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	 if you find the intestine tied with the thread, untie it, and push the intestine out of the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	 And if you find the boil, take it to the onion, and grind off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	 And if the artery causes you problems or the vein, go there gently, then return to your work and take two needles, insert two thin wires through them, and insert the needles around what you have made in a cross shape so that you make it pierced.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	 Then hold the abscess to three leagues above the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the skin as much as possible, and separate the dead flesh from itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	 or you grind it when it is soft and can be pierced, then treat it as necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 Draw out the blood or the moisture that you find, then treat the place as needed, and bind the place.
dou chancre	of the abscess
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	 We have described in the section the likeness of a scab, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how to remove the iron cure.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	 And let us speak about scabies in the armpit, and great caution in its treatment, and they say that when scabies is in a place where it can be shaved like a scab that is on breasts or thighs, or similar places, it should all be removed at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	 And when it is large and old, one must not approach it, for I never knew anyone to heal it.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 No one has ever healed (it) before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	 And the operations, when they are in place and can be removed as we have said, are that you cleanse the patient once of black bile.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	 then make him purge if there is apparent overfilling, then set the patient in good position to perform the operation.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	 Then wash your hands and scabs or boils, and the head of everything from all sides, leaving nothing behind.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 Allow the blood to flow freely, and anoint the place well with your hand or something else, and if the bleeding opposes the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the wound is coagulated.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then, cure with another treatment until it heals (or becomes healthy).
de ydropisie	And from the dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	 We have said in the division the similarities of edema, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done with medicine, and the one that is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	 if it is ruptured (or burst).
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	 and iron should not be touched in these two similarities:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	 that is to say, tympanites and ophisarcos, because it is a deadly thing.
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	 Therefore, when treating this similarity of edema called "ruptured," if the treatment does not help, then check whether the patient is weak or has another disease besides edema, such as distension of the stomach and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	 Do not touch with iron, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	 If you see the patient with strong strength, and he has no other disease except scrofula only, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should treat it thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 Lay the patient on his back on your hands, and the assistants press the belly leading the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the curved spoon according to this shape:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut through in two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	 at the tip, and it should not be so deep as to reach the intestine when inserted, and it should not pierce.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	 then look if the dropsy is herniated towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	 If you need to make an incision, you must cut below the belly button three fingers' width right under the navel.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	 and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the navel.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	 and if it is due to obstruction, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie on the incision so that excess fluid does not run to that weak place;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	 Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, push it and slide your hand all along the spatula between the skin and the flesh as when peeling an apple to the thickness of a nail or thereabouts.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 Then pierce the flesh down to the water level (which is the bottom), then pull it out and insert this tool here shown with its shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	 And it resembles a thin silver chain, made of tin or light iron, and has a small opening at the lower part.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	 and on one side there are three openings.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	 and one on the other side, and one on each of the opposite sides.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 and the head is cut in a feather shape, and this is the form of the incision that scribes make when cutting a quill pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	 At the top of it (the head) is the alemel, so that when the instrument comes to the water, you should now raise it on the instrument.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	 Then empty the vessel (or the third part of it), because if you look at more than necessary in that hour, accidentally, the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will faint, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	 but empty according to its strength and according to the indications of the patient's condition and pulse.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	 then pull the instrument and hold the water, it is now held for the caution that stops the perforation which is on the cyst, as I have spoken about, you pierce in this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	 Then begin the instrument again on the other day if you see the patient suffering and draw a little amount of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 Do it every day, but do not let it heal too much, just a little bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	 If you doubt about the patient and let too much water, then cure it with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint it with wine.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 and heal it with drying medicines until it is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after removing water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the vein
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born who do not have foreskins at the penis, or the foreskin is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If it is necessary to pierce through all the spittle very thinly according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	 then put or pierce the small hole in the bladder and bind it for three or four days until it wants to urinate, then remove the holes, make it urinate, and then return.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 And by chance it should not [be so], because the urine that comes out does not keep it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 For the person whose ulcer is small, it is treated with a poultice of cloth, as we have said, and it will open up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	 Those who have no opening in their place are bladdered, because none are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, therefore they cannot urinate unless they lift up their penis.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 And they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the marriage bed, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	 The way of the work is that the patient lies with his back on the ground, and places the head of the penis and the base in the same position as a feather's tail, so that the opening is open, as required.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And beware of the flowing out of blood that happens often, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from those who are bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the genital sores
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	 Many times, this ulcer appears on the penis, it is an appearance of ugly sores.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	 and some are malignant and some are not malignant.
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	 You should gently take them one by one with a fine linen cloth, then strike and clean them all, and put cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment on top.
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the ulcer is malignant, with pus-like color and swelling, then you should apply a fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	 When you have struck it, and the ulcer is in the foreskin of the penis with part inside the skin and part outside, then you should remove the ulcer that is inside first.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 And when it is healed on the outside, heal the inside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	 For when you heal it together, the genitals of the penis are not guaranteed to not be pierced, and blackness and decay come into the penis and testicles.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary to burn everything that is black and corrupted, then lay it on a plaster of honey and flour which is made from the peel of pomeranate seeds and vine leaves, and then heal it with other remedies until it becomes healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if there is discharge of blood, bring the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	 The cautery aids in these conditions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	 this means the evacuation of blood and corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	 if the head of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, it is necessary to insert or have the patient urinate through a reed cane.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	 if the foreskin is torn on the head of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to injury or abscess, then you must shave it with an instrument, removing the skin until the ligaments are released and the penis is delivered from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	 And if it is painful to speak of this, you must cut off a small piece from the tip of the rod and skin.
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 Then squeeze them well together, and place a thin linen cloth dampened with cold water between them so that they do not stick.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	 Circumcision is not simply the removal of skin as in other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 However, when we perform this work of our own will, and specifically for infants, it is necessary to make the best work, and the easiest one for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients would not circumcise their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	 For I have observed that most of the masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around that time, used force and cut off too much.
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 If the hairs are fleeing because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is struck and the other below remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	 Or cover it up again, and the pain is doubled, and at the amputation that is deep cutting of the member is not assured.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 And at the amputation of the nail by chance escapes the iron, and spoils the work, and many times it grows so that there is no need for amputation, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found the advantage of using ligatures in amputations, because the force cuts equally well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	 For when you hold your hand, you cut equally at all times.
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	 but that the thread be well tightened around the skin.
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 And the method of the first operation is that you make the child think, if he can understand, that you do not make him pull on the thread around the rod except just so, and then let him play in all ways as he can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	 Then make it be between your hands straight, and press the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the infants cannot see, nor any of the tools.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	 Then place your hand at the shaft and blow or spit, and pull it up until the head of the shaft is out.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	 Then clean it well of the filth that has gathered, then tie the end point with a double thread, then tie it under the buttock to another thread.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	 and hold it according to the second tie at the pocket and the index finger, and press between the two threads, then pull the buttock quickly and draw the head of the shaft.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	 Then let the blood flow freely, for it is the medicine.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place powder on top and on the powder apply a glue made from cooked egg white steeped in rose water, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, leave it on until the next day, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	 The form of forces for healing is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The two shoulders are tender and sharp, and they are as big as the fist equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	 The error of mundification is when the kidneys within are incised.
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	 Therefore, it must be spread with your nail so that the flesh becomes an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 And press equally, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then hold it with pliers, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	 If they pass more than three days, and what is below the waist is swollen, then leave it until the abscess subsides, and gently scrape it.
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 Press as much as you can move, and keep away from the part of the waist, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	 Therefore, treat the joint of things solidly closed wounds with powder, as we have said or treated powders, and if you apply too much heat, it will not help;
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 therefore, heal it, as we have said, when it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	 The retention of urine is by obstruction of stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or snow, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	 and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is due to a stone in the bladder or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	 and let him place his feet on the back, extend his abdomen from above the lower back, and restrain the patient as much as he can.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	 And then, the flanks of the bladder are compressed towards the piercing of the stone above, so that the urine is expelled.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	 If it does not come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must provide extraction with all the instruments called "syringe", of which this is its shape:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And it should be of fine silver, thin and light as a bird's feather;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 And the cane should be one and a half palms long and fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	 And the manner of urine expulsion is to take a double thread, tie one end of it to a piece of wool or cotton, and insert the other end into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	 and remove the surplus of the thread and insert it up to the tip of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a chair, and rub the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and cold water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	 Then gently insert the syringe into the rod, until it reaches the root of the rod, then double the rod upward towards the buttock.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	 Then insert the syringe up to the bladder and make the patient feel it reach the empty place. This is not done according to this order, unless the person guiding where it goes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	 Then thread the string through the wool strands one by one, and let the patient urinate while doing so, then pull out the string and straighten the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorchures or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medicines, do everything with the instrument called "clepsydre," and its form is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	 It is closed (or blocked), and if it has been pierced three times:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	 It from one side, and it from the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	 and the joints closed by this way so that the medicine rod can stop the worm well without addition, if it can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	 and when you see to throw your medicine into the bladder, place the head of the cuestor in the moisture, and draw out the one that is there;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	 if you draw out the moisture with the cuestor, and then press forcefully on the wound;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	 if the worms enter into it (the cuestor), they will go to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	 and this is the form of the subtle suppository with which one treats the bladder:
si est ci:	 If it is here: [No direct translation as 'si est ci' is a conjunction meaning 'if it is here', not a sentence itself]
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	 And it is of silver or lead, and the head is higher.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	 and beneath to the breast or the ligament falls down.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	 Then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you use to treat the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good thread double, and heat the bladder full of that moisture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	 Then push the head of the bladder into the penis, then hold your hand on the bladder full of that moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	 and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle, pierce it roundly.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	 Then insert the strong thread into these wounds, then form a circle like one forms a needle, and put inside it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and bind it in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 and do as you have done with the bladder, press it with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	from cutting into stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	 We have said in the division of stones, and their extraction together with medicines.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	 and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in meat and all the signs, and in which stone one should work by cutting.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	 and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	 I say that the stone embedded in the bladder happens more often with children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	 And he opens the hernia, greatly irritates the patient's penis, and pierces it multiple times before bandaging.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	 And from such foundations, the treatment arises.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	 And children's healing is light until they are four years old, and it is very serious in the elderly, and moderate in those who are between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 And the healing of those with large stones is lighter than that of those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes blocks the stone (arrow or bullet).
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	 Then take the patient by the feet, turn him upside down, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and shake it one or two times upward.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	 Then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely descending downward.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	 Then press and touch inside [the dislocated joint].
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 If you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	 And if it does not fall with the touch, wet your left thumb with oil, if the patient is an infant, or moist your finger, if the patient is a young man [or adult].
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	 And push it into its foundation, press the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it out of the bladder.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 Then press upwards with your finger, and push it to the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	 Instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to stretch out his right hand towards the opening of the incision, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the openings in the place where the cutting will be done.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 Then insert the large spatula of this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	 And place it between what is between the cheeks (of the buttocks) and the base, not in the middle but along the left side of the naval.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	 And it should be straight above the stone (pierced by the arrow), and your hands should be at the base or the ground, and the end of the spatula along the width of the wound so that it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	 By chance the pressure of your hands that are at the base may cause it to leap due to effort.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	 And know that there is this stone or one with edges and margins:
si est griés a issir;	 It is tightly closed.
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And if it has this shape, round like a plum and hollow, with the exit being light (or easy).
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	 For him then where there are angles and edges, make the cut larger.
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	 and if it does not jump out, then you must use pliers similar to a chisel at the top, in order to press down on the stone so that it does not slip.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	 or you push underneath the instrument curved slightly towards the top.
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	 and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, then enlarge the hole slightly with a drill bit, and if it does not break open, stretch it with glass.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 and if there are more than one stone, push the largest towards the bladder neck first, then strike it, pull it out, and pull out the smaller ones afterwards if there are more of them.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be made larger by making a bigger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	 For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	 either he dies, or urine comes immediately through where the loins cannot be joined.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	 but nevertheless make an effort to drain it, or break it with pliers, until you draw it out in pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	 and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, and bandage it, then lay on top a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in olive oil and cold water or rosewater, to cool the inflamed abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 then lay the patient on his neck, and do not unbind the ligature until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen [the bandage], moisten the wound well with oil and water, then apply the ointment defyndicon and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	 If an abscess or corruption comes in the wound and freezing of blood in the bladder occurs, causing urine to be retained, which is known in this way without jump with urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	 Therefore, push your finger into the wound and draw out the blood, for if it remains there, it will cause the bladder to swell and burst.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Then clean the wound of pus, dirt, and linen, and aid it in all ways that you know, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And it is necessary to tie both thighs when you treat him, and apply the remedies on the appropriate place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	 If the stone is small, it should be guided by the sperm and inserted with a probe, and if the urine cannot exit.
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If you treat as I have said, cut it many times; he will be excused from the punishment due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork according to this shape and sharpened at four angles on one thong:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	 Then take the thread and tie it around the shaft of the arrow under the stone, so that it cannot return into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	 Then gently push the awl into the shaft, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	 and turn the awl in the stone slowly, bit by bit, until you can pierce the other side of the stone;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Soon the urine will come, then press your hand on what remains inside the shaft that is within the stone;
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	 It will soon break and jump out with the urine, and the patient will be cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	 If you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread under the stone and the other above, then insert the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And heal it until it is sound.
de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone (meaning: uterine stones or ovarian cysts)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	 If a stone should be introduced into a woman, and if such a thing happens once, it is a grave harm, and it is forbidden for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	 the first reason is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 And the second is that it cannot be found a woman who knows well how to uncover herself in front of mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	 And the third manner is that unfortunately one cannot find a woman who knows well in this art of hands.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	 And the fourth manner is that the woman's stone (womb) is deeper than the man's, so it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear. If it is necessary to do this, you must take a skilled midwife, but if one cannot be found, even an experienced chaste maiden can be used.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	 and presents a wise bailiff in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands her to do what you command concerning the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	 And look very well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	 Then one must put his hand or foundation and feel for the stone.
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 If it is found, one should hold it under his hand and advise her to put her hand or press on the sick spot with her left hand on the bladder area.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	 If it is found, she should move it gently in and out from the bladder entrance to the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	 Then strike the stone against the root of the thigh towards the middle of the bone, where it is moved and feels the stone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	 And don't move your hand above or below the stone, and it should be cut in the first small piece.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	 Then push the shoulder towards the waist, if you feel the arrow is close to the wound so that the arrow can come out easily, and know that there are many types of arrows.
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 This means, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, and those with barbs.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 Recognize the symptoms to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	 And if the arrow escapes, put broken vitriol at its place and hold it for an hour until the wound is cauterized.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	 Then return to your work until the arrow is out, and have tools that I told you for extracting the arrow in men's help for you.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	 And if the arrow escapes and it is the artery that is cut, put powder on its place and hold it with straps and bandages, do not try again, leave the arrow and do not pull it out, otherwise the patient may die.
puis cure la plaie.	 Then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is relieved and the wounds have healed, return to your work until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	 Gravel is nothing but an accumulation of moisture or white chalk that is under the eyelid, which contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	 and is called "white chalk", and sometimes it is properly within the egg's membrane, if one believes it to be another egg.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	 and it is the eyelid's skin between the white chalk that we have said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this aquose is due to weakness that comes from the kidneys, and this matter is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	 And sometimes it comes from a blow on the eyelids, and this moisture can have many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	 or it is yellowish discoloration, or without redness, or black, or white watery, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And these are the signs to recognize this assembly; for if it is as white as we have said, then it is an abscess, long like the shape of an egg, and does not open its eyes, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	 And if there is moisture in the very cloth, then it is an abscess like part of an egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	 And if the moisture is between the skin of the eyes and the white as described, then it can be easily felt.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, prove it with all the intrusive pressure, so that its form is as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this which follows the intrusion, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	 And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be purified to the extent of our power and the fullness of his body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	 Then place it on its back, on a small raised object, and put many cloths under it.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	 Then lay it on its left side, and instruct the attendant to sit on its right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs of the neck.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	 Then take the spatula of lard, and cut the hide of the neck along its length until you reach the base, making your incision straight through the skin up to whitish fat, and peel it off gently according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	 Then make a large hole in the whitish fat with water, drain all the liquid, and then put your fingers in, and lift the whitish fat.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	 And do not touch the heart of the kidneys, but only the bladder.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	 Cut or in pieces delicately the ribs of it, because if you do not cut it skillfully, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	 And if the egg jumps in your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work with the bladder.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then assemble the two kidneys at one stitch, then heal it as with other wounds, until it heals.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	 And if you find the egg corrupt from another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, suspecting the discharge of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 Then cut the kidney with all the suspension, and draw out the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	 And if an ulcer is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches.
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	 If the other part is joined as you have done with the first, equally, then suck out the blood, and put in the wound moistened linen in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 and place another moistened linen in wine and oil on the two openings, and put over them coverings, and tie it above all the thread that is according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	 Then take two coverings, use them of woven linen according to this appearance and assemble them by sewing in the girdle of the braies, and one of the heads take up on the foundation until the back, and the other at the part of the handle.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	 And the other bone of the two upper chiefs, and all is gathered together in the loop of the collarbone;

et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	 and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the knees
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	 Check that in the section of this remedy there are many variations in its preparation, which makes it seem that it is more effective to leave it as it is.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 And I will tell you the work and the similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	 Many abscesses come in the body, and particularly in the bones;
et c’est par mout de cas.	 And it happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	 It is due to excessive sour and acute fluid spreading in the joints or from impact.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	 The color of the abscess follows the color of the body.

Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	 When it is due to an artery, it is known by the hot composition of abscess when you press with your fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 And you should not touch it.

et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 And if it is outside the white part or in the vessels within, you must release all that softness and crush it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the placenta is on the back side, then you must crush the whole thing and draw out the egg, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscesses of the knees
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	 This is an abscess wrapped in an envelope resembling a boil, with the softening of the necks, and the patient becomes very quiet when he goes.

de la routure dou syfac	From the cutting of the siphac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	 The outcome of this incision is by the opening where pus comes out, or the extension on the belly in the area of the inguinal region, because the intestines descend through that incision to one of the eyes (opening);
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	 and this opening is either the pus-producing area, or the extension of it, and these two ways of death come from multiple causes:

And the symptoms are when it is of the section where the intestines are cut open, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscesses appear variously beneath the skin near, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body expelling them through the opening of the incision.

de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dares to heal by iron.

dou chastrement	The correction or punishment

des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	 Hermaphroditus follows these two ways among humans:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 one way is when the two testicles are open as in the figure of woman's nature, where there is hair and sometimes in court he urinates.

Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	 And the healing of man and woman is such that you bandage all the adjacent sores, and heal them as other wounds.
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 In the second manner, of men whose urine jumps through the scrotum skin, has no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tension
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	 An ulcer is an adjacent sore on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the healing.

et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 And to another sore that arises at the mouth of the wife, and it swells, and by chance jumps forth, and is similar to a cowpox, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease".

de erratique	Of the dislocated joints
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	 And errhine is when the nature of the woman is not perceived or the wound is small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	 It is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that comes upon it.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	 Or it is a sore attached or shallow or deep, and is caused by fullness in the wife, or in the sides, or under, wherever it may be.

Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the obstruction is close to appearing, either at your hand or at your side.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	 If it is a small ulcerous sore and it is near the livestock, hurry and treat it thus:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	 Put your two index fingers together and have her lie on her back, with legs spread.
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	 then form the two livestock so that the ulcerous sore becomes round and is covered by the lips.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 then take wool, wet it in oil, and put it on the sore, and make her lie down each day so that it does not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 If it is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula resembling the leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	 If the covering is new flesh, press it at the onion and pound it.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	 and prepare the remedies to stop bleeding, such as cucumber juice, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with many eggs.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	 Then bring a broad strip of linen, so that the wound does not close.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	 and make it long, and bring a dry tent of linen.
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal with other remedies until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in marriage snow comes, it should be covered in this manner, unless abscesses are aggravated.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For to the aggravated abscess in marriage, one should not touch to do it.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins, which without cord usually do not close, and when hemorrhoids become old they swell.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 And we have said in the division the similarities of them, and the signs, and I will tell here those which receive healing.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and throbs, when they are full in marriage, and do not appear to touch, should not be cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the mouth of the vagina, they can be felt, are those which one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	 Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold house, then pull out the swelling with tweezers at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicine that stops blood, such as cinnamon and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	 Then press his feet against the surface for an hour, then immerse them in cold water.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 And if there is bleeding, make him sit in a decoction of sumac bark, pomegranate rind, ivy and similar things, then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and apply it as a poultice on his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if bleeding stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	 If that doesn't help, make him wear cupping glasses on the back and around the breasts without cutting.
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 Then take linen cloth, wet it at the bottom with plantain or marshmallow juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And when the abscess has healed, treat the area with ointment until it is clean.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	 And that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, if it needs to be covered as I said, cover it with lard.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	the abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many kinds of abscess come in marriage (a metaphor for the body), such as carbuncles, painful abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	 Therefore, in this treatment, I will explain the hot abscess that comes in the marriage which is not the kind of abscess that wraps around.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 And if you wish to know the work of iron, look whether the abscess is hard at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	 Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it die until the pain is alleviated;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	 Then make the patient sit on a chair, or two chairs where he can lean, and support his back and place his feet at the sides away from the leg.
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	 Spread out his thighs, put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong rope.
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	 Then apply the bellows towards the right side, and bring the instrument used to open the bladder, from which follows the form.
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	 It is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you first pierce the right side to know the depth of the bladder, so that what enters inside from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient.
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	 And if the wound is deeper, it should be covered with linen cloth to prevent pain.
