Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	 The second way of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is like anyone who join two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the suture to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	 Insert an awl or end of the mirror nearby, and pierce that spot only, leaving the two ends of the suture.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	 Then turn the awl and pierce it from the outside to the inside through both ends of the suture.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	 Then pierce one and the other from the outer part to within, in the two shoulder blades that are opposite each other.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 and this is the twisted method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	 Galen said this word, and no one disputes it, that the belly should be stitched with two needles, where there is thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	 and one needle should be thrust from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew gourds.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Know that when the wound is within the belly, the stitching is more difficult than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	 The judgments of the wound are as those of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	 And it is that when you find the fresh wound filled with blood, as soon as the arrow has moved it, then return the intestines and the bowel.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	 Then put a healing powder on top of it, and if the arrow has moved it, then put any available ointment on it until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	 and sew the flesh, join the sides, and mend the wound.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then heal the wound as with other wounds, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if you have no medicine, put old cotton on it as soon as it begins to ooze, move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	 For you need no other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	 And if you doubt that the wound is spreading to the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten a light linen in warm oil or rose oil, and put it around the joints, and beneath the saddle.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	 If it feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and it often occurs, then clisterize with black wine, and especially if the putrefaction comes to the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 and pierce it inside, know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "yew" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the planting of veins in them, and the subtlety of the entire body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	 And if the worm jumps from the wound, put it back as the intestine does, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	 And if it is old and turned or black, you must cut the black area, so that blood does not come out of it, for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 Then cut the part between the ligament and hold both shoulders hanging from the bottom of the wound to align the extraction when the arrow falls out, and the wound is opened.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	 When the intestines are cut and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, as I have seen that a man was speared or pierced with a lance through his abdomen.
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	 and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it became an abscess and turned into a fistula, and in it there was excretion and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 I will treat him according to what I know, and I will not stop refining it until he is well, and the limbs are joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	 And when I see them joined together, I doubt that the patient does not have illness in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	 and it had no illness, but waited for better conditions, and food and drinks.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	 And the experienced ones said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	 Take large threads and then gather the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened the mouth, place it on top of the two lips so that it pulls out.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	 and then press the head, holding it so that it cannot separate, and put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is all captured.
et cout la plaie.	 And dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	 If the head swells in the intestines and brings no harm to the patient, and the intestines can be tied with a thin thread cut from the intestines of an animal, as follows:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	 Take the head of this thread from the intestines and tie it to the head of a thin linen thread, then put the thread into the needle, sew the intestine and remove the waste in the incision.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	 And this method of stitching swellings is not without risk or hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 And if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the internal intestines, there is no remedy or health, unless through subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or when it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called "fistula", and equally when it opens and swells up.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	 And fistula is hard and white knot-like nodulation where there is no pain, and it is as hollow as a bird's feather.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	 sometimes clear-bright hollow, and other times thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	 sometimes shallow, and other times quite.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	 and I have spoken about it in the section on wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, this is not due to anything but one of the NINE causes.
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	 namely, because of the small amount of blood or body;
ou por sa malice;	 or because of its badness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	 or because there is hard flesh inside it, and above the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	 There is too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	 The joint is paralyzed, and the material is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	 The medicine is not good in the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	 Because the corruption is a kind of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	 The property in the region slows down digestion, and health delays, and it naturally dissolves slowly.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	 There are veins or bones.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I will tell you the cure for fistula that is made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	 Fistula occurs in all members of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	 Because fistulas come from large veins, arteries, nerves, the small intestines, the bladder, any of the ribs, the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 And if it comes to the property of the main member, or similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	 All such fistulas are of grievous healing, and there is but labor and ignorance in it.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	 And if there is any fistula that does not come up to the level I said, and you have faith in its cure, and you know it, take a tent of wax or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	 And if the fistula is twisted, seek a subtle tent of lead, for lead bends with the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	 And if the fistula has many openings and you cannot seek it with tents, clisterize it through one of the openings, for moisture is so short from one opening to another, and cleanse it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	 Then press gently to your power, so that you know if it is bone or nerve, and if it is hollow, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	 and when you know truly where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I told you, cut according to what I told you, and remove the fracture and the corrupt flesh that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	 and then cure it until it is healed, and if the abscess is deeply perforated in the correct place, you must cut to the bottom as much as you can, then put dampened plugs filled with medicinal ointment into the fistula, up to its head, so that the ointment corrodes the superfluous matter that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And then put on linen bandages clean, until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 If it does not heal by this means, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the wound, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	 If neither veins nor nerves trouble or main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	 and if the bone is exposed and there is rot and blackness, as long as all the rot is removed, then treat it with clean linen bandages until it heals;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	 If it does not heal and bends as before, know that you are not yet at the fountain.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	 if exposed and cut until you reach the bottom, remove all rot, then reset the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 And if it [the joint] is in this state, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	 If not, know that the corruption is too far advanced, you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	 if there is no other device than letting it heal naturally.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	 and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can extract with tweezers, take it out using the suitable instrument for that purpose, and if there are several bones, take them all out without leaving any.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, press, moisten, and warm the area, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	 If you cannot remove them within an hour, place something stimulating pus on the wound and wait until the flesh grows around the bones, then they will be removed more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	 And if it is a large bone, as in the leg or thigh, press on the corruption only until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	 And if there is much corruption and it reaches to the bone marrow;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	 you must be covered with linen until the corruption stops spreading, and then heal it.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And I will tell you about a fistula that occurs in the thigh bone, so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	 There was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to something coming from within his body, causing matter to come to the leg, and he had a large abscess that could not be opened.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	 But the madmen overworked [the affected area] so much that the abscesses opened, and they were full of matter, and it became a fistula, and many pustules came out that leaked both pus and moisture from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	 and many madmen put a cure around it for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing as I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the medicines that were used to treat him, and what ran out through the pustules at great length.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 And the young man's body became red, and he had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I inserted a tent in one of the wounds, and then I sought all the wounds, and found that some came towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	 I quickly went there, and covered one of the pustules until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	 I was appearing to me as the corrupted bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption except that which I left.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	 and began to treat the wound with salty medicines for long times, but could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	 and then I began again, exposed the bone as before, found continued corruption in the bone, treated it, then left it, and tried to heal the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	 but I could not go around the bone with my hand, and took it all out by its socket, then treated it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 and it became healed and solid quickly, and there was no need to start the work again except due to the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and due to my fear of death for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation often bloodied, but it became entirely healthy, and grew in the bone a hard cyst, and was of good condition and had no harm or contrary to anything at all, neither on the outside nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	 And if a bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	 Take a splint, and hold the end of the broken bone open, and command someone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	 and place another thicker splint over the muscle that is torn away from the bone, and hold it in place, extending the fracture so that you pull out the damaged muscle beneath, exposing the bone where you wish to be, ensuring it does not pierce the skin.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	 and place iron or a plank under the bone to protect the damaged muscle;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 it must be set as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and be held in place again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	 And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it, uncover the flesh entirely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	 Then place the brand beneath [the affected area], and then sew the one part of the corruption to the other, and let the length of the suture be equal to the length of the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	 And if the corruption is in the joint, then break the corrupted joint and connect the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	 And if the corruption is between two joints, then there is no remedy but to cover it over.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	 And if the corruption is at the base of the hand or the foot, it is a great difficulty, but nevertheless you must investigate this corruption and find out how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	 And clean it in all ways that you can, but let neither vein nor nerve hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	 And know that the incision and the saws for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	 And therefore, it is necessary to prepare the appropriate tool for each type of work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	 And know that the work will show you the tool you need, according to knowledge of this art, and the experience of the types of diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 Choose the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	Hot iron
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	 The shoulder may dislocate either internally or externally.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	 And when you have treated that corruption through the use of medicines, and they are of no benefit, it is necessary to cover that member as far as the place where the corruption occurs, so that the patient may escape death by this or by the greater evil, which is the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	 And the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption of the limb spreads from limb to limb and attacks the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 If you hurry to cover it, and if the corruption is in the head of the hand, as from the sting of certain venomous creatures such as scorpions, sea vipers, or similar, cover it and do not give it any space to reach as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	 And if it reaches as far as the hand, strike at the joint so that the rot does not reach the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	 If it comes to the elbow, strike at the edge.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	 if it passes the edge, that's death, and no treatment outside the quantity of its power is of any help.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	 And act thus when the rot comes or the wound weeps:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	 If it comes at the first joint, then you strike after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	 If it comes in the foot, then you strike throughout the entire foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	 If it rises in the leg, then you strike at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	 If it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy for the patient but death.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	 The method of striking or soothing the limb is to bind it above and below, and stretch one of the ligaments downward, and another ligament upward, and you cut through the tissue between the two ligaments with a spatula wide enough for the bone to be exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 Then strike or soothe, and place a piece of linen on both sides, so that the blow does not touch the healthy part, and bring another injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	 And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the area immediately, or apply some restraining powders on it.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and heal it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	 And I will tell you what happened to the man in my opinion:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	 A man suffered a burn that looked like fire scorching, and the scorching began first in his foot, consuming it completely.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	 And when the man saw the scorching, he cut off his foot, and he was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	 And long after that, the scorching returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I treated him with things that repelled it after the cleansing of his body, but the scorching could not stop.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	 And he commands me to cut off his hand, and I will not unless I have hope of affecting the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	 Also, he doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the vitality of man is weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	 And he completely gave up hope and returned to his land, and armed himself to cut off his own hand, and he recovered.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And I have never heard of this happening except in the case that it is done differently if needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	 An abscess appears in a charred place and remains for such a long time that it causes a large swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	 Then it bursts and breaks open, and the abscess liquid flows out, leaving the wound exposed like a knight.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	 And the skin that is above is as subtle as the fabrics unraveled, and it will not reach the bone nor the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain", and not "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	 but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in full depth, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	 and the skin is such that you must cut all around it, and similarly when it is subtle, as a fabric.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 and it does not burst due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	 And if you suspect that the skin will burst, and the corruption is not in full depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, treat it with clysters as follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	 Look to see if the breasts are large, and if they smell bad, then apply Egyptian-made clysterization (enema) in this manner:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	 take asafetida, oil, and litharge equally, cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine is red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	 and then take from this according to your need, make it into water and honey, administer the enema to the breast, and restrict the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	 leave the medicine inside for two hours, then draw it out by straining it.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	 do this many times until the breast is purified and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	 and sometimes an enema of ash should be used when this medicine is not present, and you take vine-wood ashes, pour water on it, let it boil, then strain it, and administer the enema until you know that the breast is purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	 And if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine, nor the water of ashes, then let him be cleansed with water and honey, or he may have a little powdered licorice.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	 let him be cleansed with honey and sweet wine, for the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine makes the wound heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	 and when you have done this, and you are confident that the breast is well cleaned, then let him be cleansed with what causes milk to grow in it, and take a medication made from fennel, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	 let him be cleansed with various medicines and ointments, whose properties or treatment of wounds I have mentioned.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	 And if the wound of the breast is small and the cannula of the clyster does not enter it, enlarge it with a knife a little, and put on it an Egyptian ointment or Basilicon ointment until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the wound is too wide, allow it to heal naturally so that the cannula or clyster may enter, and if it discharges pus above, lower or press it down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	 For when the wound is deep, do not let pus collect inside.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	 And if you cannot cover the wound below as desired, arrange it in such a way that the wound drains downwards, because when the wound is deep, do not let pus collect inside and if you cannot cover the wound below as desired, arrange it in this manner.
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	 The first part of the bow moves gently downward, and do not let anything from the bow go.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	 Take medicines that strengthen and put them on the wound, and lay a linen cloth over the entire wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	 Then press the wound towards the breast, a little larger than the first one, then apply ointment gently on the other cloth according to the size of the wound, and place it over the wound in the chest to align the bow, do not remove the large cloth for several days after some time.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	 And the one on the wound in the chest often removes it to remove the bow, and knows what moves from the bow, if it is poison or pus or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	 And take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises on the wound of the blood, then know that the breast is pierced already, and approach the healthy.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Then undo it in the morning or midday, and when you undo the wound, change another cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts sag due to indigestion after many days, know that they will not correct themselves.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison spreads for a long time, do not despair of health, because health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	 For there are men who delay applying linen in their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	 And if he bends the breast improperly after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	 And if the breast takes a long time to heal and is distant, apply drying medicines in substance and wet in effect, such as ointment drying, for there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last remedy.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	 Take care of the liniment diligently, and prepare it with rose oil, and mix an equal quantity of old wine in it.
puis le confit et en use;	 then heat it up and apply it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	 And the same procedure works better when liniment is not available. You can take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them into a powder, and sprinkle it on honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	 Then you wrap the cloth around it and place it on the breast. Sometimes a long-term philosopher or the root of celestial lily is administered, which is like the flour and cinnamon.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	 and apply simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	 grind them, make powder, and sprinkle on the honey I mentioned earlier, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	 And if the wound is deep and not treated with this cure, then know that corruption has occurred completely, and it presses on the bone, or the tendons;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 If the treatment for fistula, as we have said before, is used.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess at the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	 Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or by chance arises in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	 When it withers and no care is taken, the abscess bursts out, and runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and possibly all of it.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 And the corruption reaches the bone until there is a stinking pain, and the toes are swollen, and the color is darkened.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When treating it as we have previously mentioned in the section, and if the treatment does not help, you must cut away all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	 The cautery is very great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is whole.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	 and if the nail penetrates the flesh below it and begins to swell and blister, you must place the iron under the nail so that it does not penetrate the skin, and push it upwards, and strike the swelling gently and lightly, and apply the remaining charred material with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then cure the wound until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike and draw out the infected material because as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	 And if you see two bones corrupted, strike them with the same force as before, then cure it until it heals.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	 And if it is wounded and stabbed, causing great pain, then you must bleed it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	 Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula, slicing across from above, and ensure that the cutting does not reach the skin beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if it happens, put something on it to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The deafening pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One must align the fingers that are born in some men by chance, which are entirely flesh and sometimes contain tendons or bones, and occasionally nails; and none of these grow from the root of a joint, but they grow in some parts of the hand or in the knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	 A newborn who is born from the uterus does not move, but one born at the joint of the thumb may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	 The cutting of a fat person is easy in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	 One born at the root of the joint is difficult to treat:
si te tien dou coper.	 Cover yourself.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who grows or should grow in the last finger, it is necessary that you cut the round part up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously, swelling in the joints comes from birth, or from injury of the wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	 You must cover that sore, causing it to repair according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	 Then place between two linens or cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick together.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Or you put between two thin boards, until the wound is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of its two (joints) comes with the palm, then strike that weld as necessary.
des vils	 of the simple folk
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	 These are large veins filled with melancholic excess that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 And it happens more often in the legs of those who walk and work or carry things, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should sometimes administer purge of bile, and then heal the basilica (abdomen).
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	 The iron cure is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	 One is to strike them, and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 And another way is to open the vein, and draw it all out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	 The incision is made in this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	 Begin the first incision with deep, hot water, very strongly, until the flesh becomes thin, then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	 then cut the vein in one of three places, with a large incision, then separate and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's strength can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	 And then tie it and instruct him to bind himself with food containing black pepper.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 And repeat the evacuation and draining when veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	 The application of this is as follows:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	 Wash the patient's leg if it has much hair, then put it in warm water, and rub the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	 And if you don't have any warm water, heat it with fire, and then apply it to the vein near the knee or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	 Then scrape the skin with a knife and strip the vein from both sides until it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	 When it is red and black, you will see that it enters the skin like a white string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	 Then push the rod in under the skin until it has risen above the skin, and then cut it open lightly at the edge, then strike it in another place 3 inches away.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	 Then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then rinse with water as you have done, and puncture it again in another place, as you have done before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	 Then make another incision, or several if necessary, then rinse it, and puncture the thigh bone, then pull and rinse until the second incision.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	 Then pull apart joint by joint, until it completely dislocates, then hold it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	 and if you cannot pull it apart or lift it, put a very thin sharp needle through its length and tie it, then push it down, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it dislocates.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	 and be careful that it does not snap back, for if it snaps back, it cannot be pulled apart or lifted, and this causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	 and when you have treated it, place over the wound wool soaked in vinegar and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and let it heal until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	 And if the wound is constricted, twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it forcefully, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And pull (it) as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	 The shape of the iron that is used to pierce the bladder is curved and does not cut, but rather it should pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 and is of large curvature, because if it is subtle, it would pierce the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	 This vein is in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry ground.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 And by chance it may appear elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to inflammation that comes from under the skin, as it appears inside the body and spreads like a snake, it pierces between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large swelling in the leg, then the flesh changes and the vein begins to protrude, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	 When the shoulder is opened, you must wind around a piece of wood from one and a half feet up to two feet, and tie it, leaving the wood on the leg, and each time it protrudes, you should wrap it around the wood again, and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	 If it is too long, cut off a part of it, wind up the remainder, and do not cover its root completely until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	 for if you cut it off, it will go back into the flesh, cause an abscess and putrefaction or evil disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	 Therefore, it must be treated little by little until the head is reached, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	 And sometimes this vein, when treated of five or ten fingers in length, a man came to me once whose it issued from ten fingers in length, and when you open it, the body or the foot bursts out and pierces through to its end.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 Empty the matter that is inside it, and bring medicine against corruption to its place for any day, then treat it as an abscess does.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	 Sometimes in this vein many waters collect, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or arm, there is much leakage, and it jumps out with a gush.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 The worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	 This disease is called in our country "cattle disease", because it often affects oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between the hide and flesh, and travels all over the body expanding and contracting, and one feels it moving from limb to limb until it breaks the skin or jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	 And is infested with putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms, serpents, and roundworms or ascariasis (roundworm infection) in the abdomen.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	 There is doubt about its malignancy, because when it goes through the body, it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	 And this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	 When you wish to cure it and draw it out, one can force it out only when it goes (through the body):
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	 Therefore, you must lie the body above and below with a strong rope tightly tied, then press on it from above and draw it out forcefully, and if it goes through completely into the flesh, and you cannot pull it out, cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	 And the greatest harm it causes is that it runs oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	 and if you see it coming or near the oil, hold the sorcerer's knot under it, then strike above and draw it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 And the patient must use body cleaning with medicinal powders to remove bad humors, and avoid eating spoiled food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	 This disease is called on our land "vakirir," and is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 And I have seen what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	 And then, the face turns upward like a worm towards the shoulder, as soon as anything else, just as living silver when it cuts from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	 The pain separates from that place and penetrates into the shoulder, and then a little afterward runs through the whole body, until it reaches the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 Then he told me that it would return around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	 Indeed, I wanted many times that pain would move from one place to another, but I did not want it, just as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	 And I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed, and for this reason appeared such constrained windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 And they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins returned. (Translation)
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	 When you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, close it immediately both above and below quickly, and then press down hard so that the windiness is constrained at its place. (Translation)
et cauterize le leu;	 And cauterize the place. (Translation)
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And if you do not see it with your eyes, cure the windiness with those who dissipate them, such as fetid pills and serapin pills, and similar ones. (Translation)
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	 The differences among them are that some have large points, small, hollow, and solid. (Translation)
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	 And of those that have two angles, and of those that have tongues, and of those where there are joints.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	 and the dislocation which occurs in any member falls according to two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 or in a principal member, as the head, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	 When it dislocates therefore in any of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you here after, appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	 if it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 and when this sign does not appear to you at all, and the arrow is not in deep, draw it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	 And the sign of the skull when an arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and a swelling appears on the head that is above the skull, is like scotomia (blindness), sclerosis (hardening of the tissues), edema (swelling), erythema (redness), inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	 and perhaps without swelling of the nostrils or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	 and perhaps it loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	 And from the wound moisture white like pus gushes out, and it also swells as if boiling with fire.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And if this sign appears to you, refrain from treatment, and withdraw the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	 The sign of the arrow when it pierces or strikes is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were thrust into a hard object, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	 And sometimes the arrow may move like a hair and produce black blood in the court, and there comes cold sweating and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 Then one must realize that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that penetrates the flesh deeply is when there is no scum discharge from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, breathes heavily and seeks a warm place.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	 If the arrow pierces the cover of the mattress, it will be deloused from the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	 and produces a great wound and great pain and sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance, something of indigestible meat may jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly or abdomen, and does not jump out through the intestinal route, there is no hope in the cure nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	 If the arrow pierces the bladder and makes it jump and causes it to flow out, and the patient feels strong pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 Know that the wound is lethal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and loin and hips and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it does not move, as I will tell you what happened to me, for this reason that you do the following:
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	 It happened to someone that an arrow or dart struck him in the root of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 I pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it came out senseless.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	 And pulled out another arrow that struck him in the oil gland beneath the paper beneath, and the arrow was bent, and could not be straightened except the tip towards the fust (shaft), and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all light weight for ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 The game was senseless, and no bad accident happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	 And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic (made of ears).
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 I was a barber, and became skilled enough to treat it, and the Christians were healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	 Draw an arrow from a man's head or abdomen, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	 but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 I made an incision over the arrow, guided it, and drew it out without any harm.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	 If a man has an arrow stuck in his back, and the wound is sutured over.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And the arrow remained inside him for a long time without changing his natural condition or causing any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	 And there was another man with an arrow stuck in his face, and the wound was sutured.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	 And it remains thus without enduring great pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	 And many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	 And pierce an arrow through the side of a prince's king who was lying in bed and was slightly leaning to one side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	 And the arrow was completely straightened out.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 I was summoned to treat him after he had lain for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	 I took great care not to feel it at all.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 And he felt a sharp pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	 I thought it was from the point of the arrow, so I placed a plaster with soothing and digestive properties on the place where there was no swelling.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 And I appeared the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	 I held the plaster for many days and healed the wound directly, and kept him like that for a long time until he felt the arrow within his groin;
et il le me dist.	 and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	 I put on the wound a healing medicine corrosive for many days until it healed, and then I probed, and felt the head of the arrow that was adhering to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	 then I probed in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	 and it exceeded the term of four months, and then the wound that I had treated began to swell, and the meat on both sides could not be drawn out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Then do not cease to refine and devise methods of instruments, until I take it the following day with well-made tweezers, as its shape will come at the end of this chapter, while drawing it out and returning the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	 And the experts judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 I will then restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	 And I have told you the quality of extracting some arrows, so place your care on what I do not say, for the books cannot grasp everything entirely.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 But wise masters compare themselves on very little things and on what is present and failing, they find new work, and new instrument, in the understanding of things strange that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	 I say that arrows do not enter the limbs where they are fixed except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	 either through the side where they enter, or from another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 and that which jumps out from where it enters is an arrow entering into the flesh, and sometimes jumps out now and then.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	 And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh is swollen around it, and the opening is widened.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	 and similarly if it is fixed in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 then it jumps out, and if it does not, pierce around it with the sharp tool everywhere that the flesh is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	 And if the arrow is driven into the skull bone and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the incidents that I have mentioned occur to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 Do not draw it (the arrow) out immediately, but leave it in until it becomes equal (with the surrounding tissue) after some days, for if the arrow goes to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not driven deep into the bone only and does not reach to the surface, and the patient remains for some days with bad condition, then try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	 And if it (the arrow) is deeply embedded and cannot be drawn out by force, administer leeches around it as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 then heal the wound until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	 If the arrow is repositioned in the body so that it cannot be seen, seek for it with all your effort;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	 And if you feel [it], pull it with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	 If the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow make it impossible to pull [it], and there is no bone, nerve or vein, open it as wide as possible.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	 Remove the arrow if possible, and if there are ears in the arrow like handles holding it in place, remove the flesh that is embedded by two parts as far as you can reach, and then break or bend the arrow's ears so that you can pull it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 Be careful not to break the arrow while pulling it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot dislocate it once, push the leg towards the joint, then draw it, for extraction will be easier in this case.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	 And if the bleeding from the wound opposes your efforts, use the remedy we have mentioned in its chapter for treatment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	 And beware of incising the nerve and the vein, and make instrument as you can pull out the arrow safely, quickly or gently; firmly or lightly.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 Place the patient according to his form when the arrow fell in, for this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the signs show you.
