Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	 The arrow that comes from another part, or it opens anything of its, or the skin is swollen near where it can be seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	 Cut therefore above, as far as pliers can reach, and then pull out.
si saut fuer maintenant.	 If it was shot from a bow, now jump on it with your foot, and if you do not have the strength to pull it out, then tie a cord around it and pull it out gently.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, then continue with the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	 If it be of the arrow shaft, push it all out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	 If it be a broken arrowhead and you wish to administer binding, give the instrument with hair, so that the point of the arrowhead enters the hair of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 Then push further, and if the arrow is covered with hair, push the instrument with point entering it, for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrow is touched, it is necessary to cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	 And if the arrow be in the groin or belly or bladder or side, and it is near and you can cover over it, do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	 And keep from cutting the vein and the nerve, then make an incision, then cut the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to remove arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	 There are many ways to do this.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The form of the buttock hair is also like the feather of a bird, to push at the point of the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tweezers for pushing and testing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	 Of veins that heal are thirty-one, hence there is a head of sixteen, meaning:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	 They are the beating ones that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbechs".
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	 and the two arteries which are in the two temples visible.
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	 and the two veins that are in the two inner corners of the eyes, which are called "aspirers".
et li voine que est emmi le front;	 and the vein that is under the forehead.
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	 and the vein that is at the head of the nose.
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	 and the two tendons which are at the neck.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	 and the two veins that are in the upper lip above the mouth, and these are called "augeheriches".
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	 The veins which are commonly known to be V in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	 The first sentence is: "One is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and lay people call it 'the vein of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	 The middle sentence is: "The middle one is called 'the artery', and it consists of the cephalic and the basilic, and lay people call it 'the vein of the heart'.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The last sentence is: "The basilic is on the right side of the chest, and lay people call it 'the vein of the abdomen', and it is above the liver, and it is that one from which blood is drawn, which opens clearly near the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	 The sentence is: "The saphenous vein is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	 And in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	 The first one is below the calf of the left leg, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right leg;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	 and the vein called "nisse," which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And there are three veins below those [veins] in the other leg.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	 The sanien vein which is after the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	 and the qualities of the sanien vein, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	 then tighten the neck of the patient to a peg, until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two places dependent on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	 Touch the place where your thumb is located, and where you feel the pulsation beneath your thumb, apply pressure on it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	 Then take the lance, push it through the vein until you reach the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein and cut both skin and vein twice through its thickness, and make the blood come out as you can see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	 Then tie and hold it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 And I have already spoken about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	 The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples is beneficial for migraines, scrofula, and ophthalmia caused by eyes filled with tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	 And the qualities of a surgeon are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	 and it stretches the neck of the patient until both veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	 and feels the pulse under your thumb, then applies pressure;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	 then pours blood from the vein on your index finger to the top, and stick the lance below, and pour the vein out, cut it, as you have done in the other two veins, and make the incision according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	 then release the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	 and then tie it securely, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 and we have spoken of their binding and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	 The draining of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the draining of the head in old facial diseases that have migrated and turned red;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	 And the quality is that the patient twists their neck to stretch it out, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 then take the tool called "fosseur", which has this form (here is its shape):
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	 And place the point on the vein, and press down with your hand (or something else), and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is clean and never use fire for the procedure.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	 Furthermore, the fire should not be too sharp (agus).
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 And the bone is displaced, because it is close; and by accident the flames break when it is fragile.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	 The sinews of the two veins that are in the eyelids help them, and at the hinge, and at the joint, and at the tendon in the oil, and at diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	 and the qualities of their sinews are such that the patient stretches his neck by twisting some rope, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Then the bone, and the sinew across, a short piece of flame, a bit wide, for there is no fat there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	 And if the flames are fragile, by accident they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 Then make a corroding of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	 The vein of the neck is useful against ague, and against dropsy, and diseases caused by heat, such as inflammation or redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	 and the quality of the vein is that the patient squeezes their neck, then presses their neck to your left hand, and takes the subtle flame long, and thrusts it into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well elsewhere, and the blood will start to flow now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	 and do not go too deep, and let the bleeding stop according to your need, then rest it for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 And this is the shape of fire:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	 The juices of the two guindages aid in the hardening of the alainne and at the beginning of boiling, and much for diseases, putrefaction, ulcers, corrosion, herpes, and stomach ailments.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	 And the qualities of the juices are such that the patient strains his neck under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	 And the master standing above the patient's head and the patient leaning on the seat, then open the vein slightly but widely, then draw out the blood moderately, as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	 Then repeat on the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently hold and close both veins so that the patient does not strain.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 Leave it until morning so the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 From the liver surgery
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The purification of veins in the mouth above helps to cool [the mouth] and promotes decay of the gums, fissures in the lips, toothache, and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	 And the quality of healing is to have the patient sit in front of you and hold their neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	 Then turn the jaw and look at both of them, the one is to the right jaw and the other to the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by the small black veins around them;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 Take hold of both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and are in doubt, take the larger one from each side, and also handle the two veins above and below, as they are the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 From below the tongue liver
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	 The healing of the veins below the tongue assists after the healing of the cervical, and it is in the restraint of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	 And the qualities of the surgeon are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he licks the tongue, and gazes beneath into each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 Then one and the other, but do not go too deep, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	 The veins of the cost side which are commonly used are often opened in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	 or by poking with all the flame of the mirtin large or olive oil subtle as you know cutting tools, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 and are large and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrhine is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	 And it is necessary to open the thick veins that contain large, turbid blood:
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more subtle, and it is for treating subtle veins that contain subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	 The basilica sainie (which is one of the veins), helps with illnesses that are under the throat, neck, breast, and stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 And it requires the lord to bleed profusely, and to empty the artery that is below;
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	 If you puncture the artery, and blood flow occurs, then it requires stopping (clotting), as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And the flame should not be pricked but cut like an onion.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	 If the basilica does not open clearly, then you must incise (open) it and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	 Or if you want any other route (vein), or bleed in the place of it from the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	 It opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And apply the fire cauterizer as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	 And if you wish to find the place of the wound, then it is necessary that you straighten the arm and touch the place where you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	 Then mark the location, tie the arm, and burn the vein with fire cauterizer.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	 And beware not to wound an artery when you see it swollen, for that is the artery.
eschui la donques.	 Avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	 And if you see swelling high as the urine of a child, and it is red and thin, know that it is not an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	 Hurry up then, and place your hand firmly on top, afterwards remove the bone without stopping its flow of blood, for this often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	 bind the arm, and let it remain in this position, and do not move it by the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	 And if the bone does not stop bleeding and it swells, and no medicine is present for you, then cut open the artery if it is open, because the head of the wound will contract.
et estainche li sans.	 Stop the bone from bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	 Take a slice of the plaster of Paris, and cut it, take one half and bind it firmly until tomorrow.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	 If the bone does not bleed anymore, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	 If not, if [you] cure [it], as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And the stopping of bleeding is not always necessary in multiple positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	 The vein in the middle helps to treat bleeding from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	 And the lord [should] turn himself towards the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deep and he finds the nerve, it swells and the wound becomes painful and may not heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	 And this nerve often opens multiple times, and if it does not open in some people due to their subtlety, then you must heal [it] with the instrument anesthetic.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 And you shall cut the nerve at your will.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	 The bandage of the head if helps, that it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 And it is necessary to bandage when pricking with olive oil or myrtle fire, because this is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	 However, you must seek the lighter joint, and do not harm anything if it is necessary for the first time, and then repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 And sometimes joints swell in some people, when it is necessary for the first time, but do not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the urine is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	 The first thing you must know about bandaging is that bandaging is not brought for any other reason than to keep health and to avoid coming diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	 And make the incision in one of the three veins that are called 'cubitus'.
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	 This means, cephalic, axillary, and basilic; (the three veins)
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	 And the incision should be made in the beginning of spring, or autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of filling appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 And the incision should be made either on the first day or the third day, after two or three hours (of the procedure).
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	 The incision for diseases does not have a fixed hour, but when it is needed day or night, at all hours and at every moment.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 And it should not be incised for children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child until the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not treat the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	 And when anyone wants to heal themselves in any way, it is necessary that their intestines be cleansed with a gentle enema, if they have retained much filth, so that the veins do not release the waste products of the intestines that can harm the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	 one should not heal who is too salty with meat or drunk, to such an extent that he farts or drools.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	 and one should not want to heal after colic pain, vomiting, stomach distention, multiplying of coitus with a woman, labor, watchfulness and fasting, and those who exhaust their strength, or by something from the weapon or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	 Then thin the fluids, if it is possible, with food and drinks and medications, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	 Then bathe [the affected area], if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood and heal the vein in the third place as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	 And keep that day from work, pain, lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	 And lie down and rest, and let the bandages be higher than those who are being healed, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently pull out the stitch above, for if it is too tight or small, it cannot heal without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	 And then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 Then moisten the punctures with a little old oil, then place your thumb of your left hand on that vein beneath the place where you wish to lance it, so that the vein does not break or split when piercing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	 For there are veins that flee like cords when pierced, and there are those that are filled with windiness, such that when flame is applied, it recoils and cannot open the vein, and this is one of them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 And if it opens the vein, the wound will be too narrow, for this reason the lancer must be aware of these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	 And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 If not, begin again a little under or above that place where it is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	 And if the area is inflamed and the patient becomes frightened, allow it to rest for a day or two, but do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	 If by chance an abscess comes;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	 Do not enter it into water, then treat the wound if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	 And if the wound is small, or the opening of the abscess is not large enough to expect as much blood as you see, trust in that same wound and apply heat directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	 Open it a little quickly, but only when the area is inflamed;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start the bleeding again, and put some oil of lilies on it, for it calms the body's blood, and in this case, the oil is its remedy.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	 And administer the oil of lilies in each bleeding that you perform, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	 and this same thing causes a triacle and boil from them when it is put on the joint.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If the pus and blood are too thick, separate them carefully.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	 If a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when the vein opening is small and the bleeding is not performed often, hurry, put moist sponge on the joint in hot vinegar and oil, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	 And it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it stays in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it will not harm [him].
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh beneath it, in a powdered form, mixed with oil, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	 Many times an abscess and appearance appear at the incision of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 Place your hand on it then, if you feel it soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	 Then do not place anything there as we have said, for it may happen without an artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 But cover the wound with dry bandages to harden it, then treat it with another remedy until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood according to its quantity based on its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	 If the wound is black, leave it to drain until it turns red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	 and if you see a large lump, let it become refined (or reduced in size).
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 and if it is hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	 For the person who is wounded and pierced, requiring bloodletting, make the wound larger and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	 And for the weak person, do the opposite, and he must be bled little by little, and it should be bled by cutting across (or transversely), not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And this method of bleeding avoids misdirection of blood and nerve damage, and is more effective than the long bleeding rather than the wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	 And to him whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give soft bread beneath green apples.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 If it is scalded, let the blood be bled three or four times; and if of a cold constitution, eat before healing soft bread in syrup sweetened, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and anise, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if it [the wound] festers at the wound site, after much bleeding, then it is necessary that he drink a broth of char, and an aromatic subtle syrup, and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if you want to fracture some bone, and heal it again as needed, when it is weakened by excessive healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if you want to fracture some bone after the first healing, and it has strong flesh, it heals seven hours after the first healing, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if you want to heal from another part, it should heal on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	 For there is much blood within the body which is already scalded and causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	 Then a large amount should be bled, and the peritoneum should be opened as much as it can choke on a cloth.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	 After you have taken care of all the conditions for healing, place your hand on top of the foot when it is healed, so that death does not come in the place of a cloth, and this happens many times when healers are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	 And it is not appropriate when you dislocate the arm, and cause blood to flow a second time, and the wounds are closed, that you press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	 And if it is curved, stretch out the arm as much as possible, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	 but leave it until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 or you pierce with the tip of the flame until the wound that has frozen shuts, and place on it a piece of linen soaked in vinegar and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is burst, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess has been soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the necessity arises to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healthier than the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	 And the method for healing is that the patient plunges their hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	 then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein is visible, then heal it now across, not wide or long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	 And let the wound be wide, and let it be cleansed closely near the joint of the hand, and if you cannot draw out [something] from there, then put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	 but if it is frozen, do not hit the hand with hot water, for one puts more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 and the cleansing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither an artery nor a nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	 The cleansing of the sheath of the right hand is effective for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it's done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	 hold the hand, and push into hot water until the vein is empty, if you can see [it];
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	 And if the wound is transverse, and you close it completely, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 And do not go too deep, because the nerves are entirely exposed bare under the skin, and then put your hand in hot water, if the blood doesn't freeze in the wound, it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as much as necessary, put oil and linen over the wound to bind it quickly, and do this with each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgative of the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I have told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The vein of the spine is effective for all diseases that are under the body, such as ailments of the back, and retention of phlegm, and diseases of the lungs, and knees and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	 And the quality of the wound is that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs it on the wound until it burns, and ties it above the ankle joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	 And the wound is at the ankle, and from above the foot there is much pain.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 Therefore, make the wound wider or larger at the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	 And if you wound on the foot, watch out for nerves that are underneath, and wound through also as in cutting;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	 and let the flames be quenched.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, place the foot in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	 And if bloodletting is necessary for the first time, begin again slightly above because the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the soothing of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The wound of the sciatic nerve is at the knee joint, and its cleaning relieves pain in the ankle, when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	 And the quality of his wound is such that the patient immerses himself or herself in water, and pulls above the ankle four fingers twisted, for otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	 and if it opens, you can bleed in all ways that you can, and across;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And it is more useful to break it [the shoulder], for the joint is dislocated, and it responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	 And if you do not reset it [the dislocated joint], no healer will open or close the door to it, and turn it towards the little finger and beware of nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	 Make such correction of the blood as you see fit, then untie the ligament [binding the shoulder], and put cotton on it and hold it in place.
ele est maintenant sanee.	 It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 open abscesses
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	 Blisters are made of horns, or hare's fat, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	 And blistering can be done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 To draw and attract blood, or to avoid wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	 And this ventosation which is meant to avoid wounding has two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	 or it is with all fire, or without fire.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	 and the ventosation which is made by drawing blood and extraction of blood is performed in 14 inches of the body, from which one is completely in the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	 and the others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	 and the others in the two sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	 and the wound under the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	 and the wound in the two shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	 and the wound on the shins.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	 and the wounds in the two arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	 and the wounds in the two legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	 and the wounds in the two ankles.
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	 And the ventosation (ventousation) does not deal with blood, except for minor veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore one should not avoid it at all, as when performing venesection (bloodletting);
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 and it should not be administered, neither at any fire nor hot iron, in any disease that comes from congestion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	 If there is a necessity to ventose for diseases, or by custom, then we will administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle, and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	 because there are some who, when they need to be ventosed, have a swollen head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	 And for those who find swelling and redness in their body, and in their head, and at the neck, and blackening of the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	 And for those who find a spot of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has swollen, and they bleed;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if there are such who have convulsions, and see blood in urine and vomit and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially if it is in the month, we order to ventose after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	 The pain of the head assists in the swelling of the eyes ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	 And this ventilation is in the place of the pain of the head, and it is not necessary for those with cold constitution to use it, or who have diarrhea, because it does great harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 And for this reason, it is not suitable at all that the watchers [or caretakers] should use [this method], nor those who have a cold head disease.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become negligent, and for this reason, the cupping glass should be placed a little lower due to the fear of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	 The ventosation [therapy] is in the location of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is effective against the swelling, and for fracturing the channel of the skull, and for all that, and for filling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 It should be pushed gently, for if it remains too tightly, it may cause obstruction in the intestines or stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	 The ventosation at the costel joints of the neck is effective against headaches, otalgia [ear pain], migraine, strangulation, and tooth root pain, and is in the location of the basilica cavity.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 And you must command the lord to press his hand to put it (the dislocation) back into place, not to cut the artery, and no bleeding should occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	 Ventilations beneath the chin are good for mouth disease, corruption of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 And it is in the place of the salivary glands of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations under the armpits are useful for diseases that originate from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	 Ventilations along the ribs are as good as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 Command the lord not to press too deeply, for the skin is bare and knows beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	 Ventilations on the buttocks are good for hemorrhoids from the base and diseases beneath, and the ventilation should be large and made of goat's hair, as it needs to draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	 And by chance, if it is delicate, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	 It makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	 The boils on the legs burst open widely because they draw blood from all over the body, and they are old sores of the rain, the marriage, and the bladder, and they reduce the flowers.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 They are located in the armpits and elbows, and despite that, they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus in various forms.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	 The way to put a boil is to first empty it, then touch it gently and quickly, stir it evenly, and not stop doing this until you see the area turn red and swell up, and make the pus appear red from blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	 Then heat (or cauterize), and apply cuppings, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are some who have cold flesh, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	 If you should cut only once, and it should be large incisions, and one deep wound.
et suce legierement.	 suck gently (or draw out blood).
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	 And if the swelling is large, then you should cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 The first time for thinning the way for thick blood to flow out.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	 And if the swelling is very thick, then you should cut a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And when we want to draw out blood drop by drop, we should only puncture once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	 And if you want a lot of blood, we will do it often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	 And if the limbs are thin, they should be strengthened fully, and the joints should be quickly pierced so that the cores are perforated; it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and those with narrow pores, to anoint the joints of the boils with stimulating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	 if it is in this case, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 and if it is in yew, with the oil of parsley, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the person to be healed has a tight and narrow wound, no oil should be put on it, but it should be washed after being lanced with rose water, cold water, lemon water, curds water, or porcelain water, or any similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from bed with the aid of aspen wood, or water of myrtle, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	 And those with thick excesses should rise from old wine, or vinegar water, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or something similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	 And it is not advisable to apply cupping before bathing or in bathwater, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And he should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he warm himself, when he needs to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	 Watch out for the one who is being bled is choleric, and let him not be too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	 He must take cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce in moderation, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 Eat light foods, such as mutton meat and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	 And the one with a cold constitution, take honey syrup, moderately fragrant old wine, and eat little, and eat light foods such as small birds and young birds and sparrows.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	 And on the day when it will vomit, it should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	 It is necessary to give certain men sometimes treacle or muscatel before or after vomiting, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And let the wine be made thin, but it is not good for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	 The vomitings that are placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, and the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and the bowels and the loins and the thigh, because these limbs do not tolerate being wounded, and it is done for nothing but to draw blood from member to member, as we do with the breasts when milking;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	 To remove the viscosity from the limb, as we place cupping glasses on the abdomen and the buttocks to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	 and remove the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, by attracting its nature through chance, or dislodge the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	 and so it is done when placed on the liver and the bladder when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to only draw blood.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 And sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleura, and so the cupping glass is filled with hot water or with water that has cooked herbs convenient for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	 And it should be two fingers and a half palm-width long, and have a hole in the middle about a thumb's width wide, like pushing an awl, made of bone, soft beforehand so as not to prick the patient when placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	 and make it through the middle a rod of bone or iron for placing a splint inside, and let them be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 for the swellings of children are different from those of the old, and thin from fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	 And this splint should be placed thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	 grasp the splint with wax or linen and place it in the splint through the hole in the middle of the splint, so that the brightness is at the bottom of the splint so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	 And then place it on the member, and your fingers should be on the sore as we have said, so that when one looks at it, if steam comes out, then open the blister.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 Then apply the thread as before, and renew it often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	 In the blister that is given in case of pleurisy, it should not have a worm nor a sore, and it should not be applied unless when it is full of liquid, and it should only be placed on the member.
et c’est li forme:	 and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	 Suppurating abscesses are not applied unless in members where blisters cannot be placed due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	 And in naked flesh, such as thigh or shin, and similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	 And the quality of the person is that when you find bladders that are in sweet clean water without purge, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	 and put them in fresh sweet water until they are familiar with it and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	 Then let them be purged of the veins and bowels, then scrub the member until it is red, and place the bladders on it;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 And when they are full and hot, if there is a place to apply a cupping glass, let it be applied, for it works well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	 If not, raise the limb above water level, and then below water, very good, and then wrap it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	 And if the limb remains too long without the body's warmth, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it on, until the pain subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	 And if the limb becomes multiple (or split), place broken glass, or gall, or similar things on it until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	 Place half-peeled beans on the limb and let them remain until they adhere to it, which will cause it to subside now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 And if you need more help, take other warm limbs.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	 And if the warm limbs do not want to take hold, scrape the limb with fresh blood or insert a needle until it comes out, then place them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And when you see them dripping, sprinkle a little bit of aloe powder and crushed seeds or ashes on them, they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	 Know, dear child, that the foolish man falls into this chapter who has never seen any of the old books, nor read any of their letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	 and for this reason, medicine is unknown in our land, as I have never found anyone good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	 I do not know anything else except through the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 I have described in this chapter what is contained therein and have summarized it at the end and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought forth, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the summary of this book, the number of words and chapters where the wise put their understanding and dwell on truth, so that those who have been proven knowledgeable will know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	 I say that when breakage or dislocation or twisting or fracture comes to anyone, it is necessary that you straighten the patient from one side and the other, if anything does not stop you, as weakness of the body, or infants, or the elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	 or if the time is not very hot, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	 and do not eat cold meat, that is to say raw or undercooked meats, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not stuff yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of an abscess heating up, nor expansion of matter in the member.
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 The patient returns with a slight movement to the first management. (Here, "governement" can also be translated as "treatment")
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make large stools, or they have thick consistency, such as cooked wheat in water, and peas, and heads, and feet, and pork belly, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment brings on softened stools and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	 And know that the broken bones of old and decayed people cannot be well recovered nor welded according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, neither those who are too tender, as in the case of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	 but there is no cure, reset above the broken bone and hold together the limb tightly until it heals as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 and do not let him at all perform his work, and for this reason, he must be fed with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breaks are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different from the break of the foot, or the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of break.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is a break that grows over time, and another that sharpens, like the quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	 And in every way he has his equipment and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes to mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	 And it is known as bone fracture because the limb is twisted, widely open due to displacement, and feels pressure when touched with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	 And if there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 But it may have twisting, splitting, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but apply medications that follow, and then hold it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	 Know that the fracture that goes in the arm and has two parts separated, you should now set them equally, otherwise abscesses will grow on it.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses grow there, leave it for as many days as the abscesses are calmed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	 Then set it equally to the motion that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 Then hold steady, as required hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	 If the bone is broken into pieces, if it's in the foot or hand, or if it's a small member, or a two-finger break, or a single finger break, using both hands.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	 And set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the limb are disjoined, you reset them with all means possible and ensure that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And align well the two joints of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	 And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	 If it is straightened well and not stretched too much or pressed as those who force it by their work to bring about an abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	 And when the limb is in place, keep the patient still so he does not move, neither while watching nor sleeping or turning or otherwise.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And be sure that the limbs are so secure that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	 For if it feels no pain, then it is not broken, and it must be put in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	 And ensure that it is placed straight, so that deformity does not come when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in smallness and largeness and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	 For there are small members such as fingers, toes, and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	 It is necessary to wrap thin and soft linen cloths around them.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	 And the large ones, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	 It is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for the broad bands embrace the whole large limb equally, and hold it tight from all sides without any gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	 Then tie light bandages around it three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and hold less, leaving a slight space from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	 and soften the bandage a little, until you take a large part of the healthy part, then take another bandage, and turn it directly over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	 then return to the part below the break, and hold moderately, not too strong nor too loosely, as we have said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 Then put between the joints of linen or cloth strips that are all even, and then bind them all together above [the affected area], and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	 And if there is an abscess or inflammation, put on top something soothing for the abscess that is hot, and which removes the inflammation, and leave it in place for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 Then bind the splints, and they should be half the width of a thick cane, or a staff used for splitting wood, or palm branches, in this manner:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	 but it is necessary that the splint placed on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	 And let it be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	 then pull up on the sutures just as you did at the first stitch, then sew it up with thread following this fashion, just like at the first break.
