plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	 the wound is narrower now, less so later.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	 and the thread should be of moderate size, not too thick nor too thin, and made of flax yarn.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 for if the thread is thick, like those I have seen in the works of fools who sew with twisted flax yarn, it is a great error, because the stitch cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each suture.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is gored by the shafts of arrows after being wounded in healthy limbs, you should place linseed oil or linen cloth on them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is fractured and the ligaments are torn apart, here is the remedy I shall tell you.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to hold splints on all broken limbs for the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	 For when the limbs are large, no need to insert arrows before five or seven days, or more according to your assurance of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	 And here is the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 And it is that you take flour that is kept near the mill walls, and mix it with abundant egg, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, on the fracture, and this is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture in various positions, and likewise for women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	 Another manner of the plaster restoring the fracture and the dislocation and the twist:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	 Take [a] probe, lancet, and tweezers and dissecting scissors and asbestos and Arabic gum, to X [the patient];
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	 Take myrrh and aloes, to V [the patient];
alechil VIIII З.;	 apply ointment VIII [to the affected area];
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	 and make powder, mix it with egg yolk;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	 if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition and quickly sets broken bones and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	 Another way of making a plaster that is effective for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	 take asbestos and lard, to X [the patient];
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	 myrrh and aloes, to VIII [the patient];
acaice VI З.;	 This sentence appears to contain a Latin abbreviation with numbers, but it is not clear what it means within the context of this Old French text. As such, I cannot provide an accurate English translation for it.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Boil Armenian bread X З, crush it well, and concoct with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	 Another method of emplaster for dislocated joints and displaced bones, and to alleviate the pain occurring, and to treat with a tool, you shall cut the bone and break it.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Take new linen, dampen it in warm water and cooked oil, and place it on the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This splint does not restore [the bone], but it is good for relieving abscess heat and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	 Another method of emplaster to heal broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	 Take dried fig leaves and earthy parsley, crush together, and make an emplaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another way to splint for the healing of the fractured bone and for encouraging the return of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	 Take root of vismalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of vetches, of each one an equal part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limb is scalded, make it with moist coriander water or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (medical plaster) stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	 Take roots of vismalve, flax seeds, thistle, lentils, and sage, as well as the flowers of violets and chamomile, in equal amounts;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 grind, and make into a paste with salt water, sweet water, or vinegar according to the heat of the limb, and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance should be placed on a broken limb for restoration except for a plaster made of beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between soft and firm but not too soft or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that dry and slightly warm things should be placed on a broken limb for restoration, such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	 Another way of plaster that is good for wounds and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	 Grind up moths and human hair, feathers of birds, and mummy, and grind them evenly, then make a paste and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	 Then after that, dissolve a little bit more, and make sure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bones moved from their place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	 But do not dissolve it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	 If pain, itchiness, lack of rest or swelling occurs at the site, hasten and dissolve it immediately, remove the paste now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	 Take a thin cloth, sea sponge moistened with seawater, immerse it in water, and apply it to the site until the itchiness stops, and the pain is alleviated.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	 Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, moistened in vinegar or rose oil, and tie it up until you are sure of the abscess heating.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	 And let the inflammation of the limb rest and the pain disappear, then resume tying it up delicately, a little plaster, and do not tighten it too much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 and thinly enough that it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that an abscess has been opened and drained, reddened, painful, and swollen, and you need emplastrum and linen, start it as before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	 And if no improvement comes to the limb in what we have said, do not loosen it until after 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	 And sometimes leave it for 20 days, as we can see, until the fracture heals and the joint approaches the bone.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	 Then it should be held more firmly than before, and the flesh should be fattened, as I said before.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	 If you see the place drying out too much, know that nourishment cannot come to it;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	 Therefore, immerse the place with warm water, every time you dislocate it, and do this for three days and let the ligament loosen a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	 By doing this, then you cut off the nourishment to the limb and hasten what the foolish man does, who keeps the limb twisted.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 This is bad, and it is dangerous work, and I see no other solution but to rest it and treat it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	In various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	 There are many ways of breaks, and various shapes, and the causes are intended for specific purposes.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	 For there are fractures that are made by sword blows, and the collar bone breaks the whole bone up to its shaft which is beneath the bone, as a crack or splinter does.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 And for this reason, such fractures are called "splintering".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	 Or if the sword strikes the bone from above causing it to pierce, such fractures are called "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	 And these two types of fractures can be either large or small wounds.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impacted percussion, cleavage, fractures from falling on stones, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the fracture penetrates through to the membrane underneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	 And if the wound is healed into the bone as thinly as a hair, and the crack is small, it is called "hairline" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	 And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or something similar, and it introduces a bone fragment into the lower part, and the fracture lines are level like a potter when making over the pots.
si entre li piere dedens.	 If the arrow enters within [the body].
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	 And this occurs more often in those who have a moist head of bone, as in a child's head.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	 and it happens in all these ways of breakage, as small pieces are disconnected, like bones.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	 I will speak about its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we shall know all ways of breakage by the dislocation above them, and the inquiry into their cause, and by the corruption of the flesh that is on top.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy resemblance is known by those who, when the bone has been uncovered and scraped above it, the breakage appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of breakage, beware of the patient's accidents; and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, paralysis, fever ague, and the eyes to come out and redden, and other similar signs in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a doubtful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the navrez comes first to you and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the muzzle.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue below the bone is corrupted, and the accidents as we have said come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	 And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must cut the split part like this:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	 And it is that you take the patient's head and expose the bone in all ways you can, and over the shape of the wound as much as you can, and if blood discharge comes to reveal the bone or abscesses appear, help him with what is needed, and it is that you fill the cavity with damp cloth soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	 And make the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed and ensure no more bleeding occurs.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	 Then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done in two ways of workmanship.
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 The first way is that you cut narrowly ahead (in front) and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then insert another cutting tool larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	 And the second method is that you have many diverse sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp-pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	 And work lightly, lest you wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	 If the bone is hard and projecting, you must bore around it lightly so as to administer sizes with drills, not piercing beyond the bone of the skull, and should have a margin or circle above the point that does not let the point pass beyond the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	 and you must have more than one, so that each comes into its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all bones.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	 and this is the shape of three types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	 The quality to pierce around the broken bone is that you place the needle on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	 then replace the needle somewhere else a little afterward, and do this all around, then cut the incision in the bone gap that is between the fractures, and do it as subtly as possible, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or any of the tools you have such as pliers, tweezers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	 and ensure that you do not touch the brain nor the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	 and when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if it is necessary that you reset the sharpness that has remained in the bone to any other tool resembling a knife, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other knives.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	 And if something remains of small bones, no scales, lightly extract them with instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 then treat the wound with linen cloths and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	 And another method of work is that which the Greeks call, which is more severe.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	 and he strongly commands, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose a part of the bone, where the open break moves, so that when you have exposed that part, you place it under the head of this lever-like instrument, as follows in shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	 And do not cut it from one side, and the parts are sharp on two sides, so that you cut towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	 then strike a small hammer on it, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 if it is pressed against the bone, lightly extract it, for you can break it senselessly and out of fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to smoothen them out afterwards, and remove the scales with a sharp rasp of various sizes, in order to provide the most suitable solution for each case, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Then pass over with a large rasp, and afterwards with smaller ones, and continue doing so until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	 In each of the other hairy forms or subtle fractures, it is necessary that you apply a remedy according to its nature.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	 and this is not something that can be replied to by him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	 And if the wound is exposed, it is necessary that you take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	 Then take another linen cloth folded double (into two or three), moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	 and do it more gently than you can, so as not to burden the wound, then administer more (linen) below, but do not strain it any more than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	 And let it rest for a day or two, until the abscesses are soothed, then release it, and administer medicines as if with lilies' roots, and barley flour, and incense powder, and Aristolochia, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	 Make powder of these things, and place it on the wound, and immediately administer reliable medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	 And ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave ointment or scabs on it, because when scabs accumulate on the brain's cloth, they will rot and cause great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 For if you place anything biting on it, it will rot from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient as we have said, it is doubtful that he will recover his senses.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	 And if blackness does not come violently except for the medicine that has been placed there, which has this effect, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, mix them with linen cloth, and apply it to the affected area.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then cure it in the manner of the treatments that are required, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	 Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	 And the one below is cartilage and does not break, unless it swells or twists, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	 If one of the two parts is broken, then you should place your little finger or thumb into the nose and align the fracture within the index finger and at the nostril exit, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And do it gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part near the neck, and the arm cannot come to its place, then you must align it with the head of a straight stick, about a finger's breadth.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	 If the break is in two parts, then do the same thing, and hurry to restore it as soon as possible if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If it is not in two parts, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, bind the wound with strips of linen on top of the head, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	 Or you bind from another side, if there is a break there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	 And the strips should be as thick as they fill the wound on the head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said to some restorer that one should moist the tents with butter, and to stir each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	 It does not seem to be good to me, but they should be moistened in the mixture of egg whites and flour.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 Wait for the swelling to subside, until the bones are hard, and the cartilages have stiffened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	 And sometimes feathers from geese are used in place of swellings, and if soaked in linen cloth and held together, the break is kept, and the patient is made to breathe.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	 or do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess breaks out while you are working on it, put either beeswax or softened cotton in oil of roses, or a pinch of turmeric.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	 If an abscess does not come out, apply a plaster on the outside, made of flour from figs and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light poultices on top, but do not bind it too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	 And if the break in the neck is small and it breaks into small pieces, take appropriate instruments for this, then make an incision, and treat with things that are healing and binding, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if there is no wound within the nails, treat it with tenets, and place plasters of linen until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured beneath and there is no wound outside, and the break is only external, but not broken in two, it is curved within, if this can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	 If the break is in the right part, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	 And if the break is in the left jaw, insert your right index finger into it gently and adjust it to the other side with the other hand, and hold evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is separated by 2, then you must administer an extension of 2 parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	 And if the teeth move or fall out, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then put cotton on the broken jaw and place a double cloth over it.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	 Place a broad and well-made cushion or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it above the muscles that you can reach, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	 And if you see that the shape changes (dislocates), dislocate it again on the third day, and then reset it to its correct position.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	 Apply a poultice on top of it (the dislocated joint), using flour from the mill and egg or meal from a plantain after you have removed the cartilage.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	 and put a light linen poultice on top of it (the reset joint), if the poultice swells, and the position of the patient does not change, leave it until it heals.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	 It often heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess swells up, bring what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	 And if there is a fracture and wound together, beware that no part of the bone is removed.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	 Use subtle instruments for the removal of the fractured parts.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, dilate it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the bone fragments and there is none left over, stitch up the wound if it is wide, and put on one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals completely.
de la forcele	From the armory (or forceps)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	 The broken bone breaks many times toward the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	 it is broken and dislocated in two places, divided into parts, and is the easiest to restore.
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	 or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	 And the procedure when the bone break is without an open wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the bone is broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	 and the other extends the neck toward the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	 then align the break with your hands so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor deviation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	 And if you need to extend further, place a round pad of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary for your needs.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And stretch and lift the limb, and hold the ball (joint) with your hand, so that you align the break as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw out the head of the shoulder by force because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and the attendant should push the shoulder forward, until the bone of the collarbone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	 Then direct the break to your fingers, and if there is a piece of bone projecting, it is necessary that you cut above it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	 and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, strike it with one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	 but place the limb under this instrument, to prevent the break from splitting apart.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	 and resemble a spoon, not concave, and be as wide as required, according to the size of the bone and the power of the job.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	 and have two handles, as you see, one wide and the other narrow, as the route of the wound that you made when treating the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And when you are certain of the abscess heat, if it opens a wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt about the abscess heat, then use linen cloths and bandages, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscess becomes cold, immerse it in rose oil and asafoetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	 The bone setting, when it has wounds and swellings, is that you put the plaster of flour and egg white on the bone, and place light bandages over it, and put a sphere under the setting if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	 Then take a very wide bandage of one palm width, then place two layers of linen cloth over the bandages, and apply the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	 Then take a thin stick of three feet long and wide, and wrap it around that bandage, leaving the ends hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	 And place the iron upon the break, turn the bend upon the neck, and sit the healthy below, and the sick above.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	 And reset it from each side, and when you see that the ligature holds the break together, and you clearly see that the iron does not move above the broken bone, then watch over it every day, and when the ligature slips, hold it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	 And make the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under his buttocks, to raise the shoulder up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	 Align the break with a sling using the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident happens, for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	 Then continue with the manipulation (of the dislocation), if it seems necessary, and hold it steady, until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 It is restored within twenty-eight days at most, and in less time for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	 It hardly ever happens that the shoulder bone breaks or moves far from its place unless it is felt by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	 If the limb adheres according to the shape of the fracture, and you reset it according to its natural form in all possible ways.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	 Then apply powder from the mill with plenty of egg and soft feathers on top of a folded cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	 Then place a large and thin stick, slightly larger than the shoulder, under which there are no hairs in any part of the shoulder, if there are hairs underneath the stick, use soft feathers of linen to pad it so that the stick is even.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	 Then hold it all in a great strong bind, so that the bone does not move from its place, and look at the ligament every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	 Whenever it grinds itself, you should straighten and align the bone if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	 And the shoulder will be restored in twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 And when this number is completed, dislocate it and be careful, because it is not the bone that easily goes out of its place again.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front, but not underneath the skin, lift it up and remove the bone, and follow what was said earlier in the setting of a fracture to treat an abscess with hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture (of the) thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	 The thighbone may sometimes be broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken in the middle, it declines below and causes the patient great pain, and lack of nourishment, and immediately vomits blood, and opens the fractures in the bones that are broken, and he feels it all very acutely.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	 The restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and you place the cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and assemble the ribs of both sides to your hands, and be subtle in aligning it in every way possible, until the figure of the bone is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	 Then place plasters and stoppers over the subtle stick of salt or another light rod, and wrap it in a cloth, and bind it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	 and twist the cord round tightly at the back, and hold it in place as needed, and check every hour if the bone has healed, and if it softens, apply pressure again.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	 and if it is necessary to release the bone due to corrosion or itching in the area, or pain or abscess, then hasten, remove the plaster, and direct those who have come for treatment.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then reset the bone until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	 Know that the break in the ribs occurs only in large bones near the back and the neck, and they do not bend except because they are slippery.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	 and it feels well at the examination of the fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the restoration is that you set the fracture equally as necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then put a splint, and tighten it with a stick if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	 And if the rib breakage is tilted downward, then the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, just as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces through the lining.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	 And it points with tips, and quickly and vomits a large amount of blood, and this is a grave sickness, and the ancients have made great effort to heal it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the abdomen in order to push out the fracture.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come if they have not arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, make them healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	 And they said that one puts bladders on the site to suck out pus, and this seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	 Every time, there is doubt as to whether the bladder will draw out superfluidities to its place due to its weak composition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say to cover the joint with damp linen in hot oil and put tents between the ribs to make it equal on all sides; then it should be cured with pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that does not pierce the membrane, and doubt is in the patient, then it is necessary to break through the rib and place an instrument under it to press on the bladder.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it should be cut open, and gently pulled out, and then the two edges of the wound should be sewn together if it is large, and it should be treated with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	 If an abscess appears, place moistened rose oil-soaked cloths on it and apply it to the affected area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it lie still in that place which needs to be incised and abscessed, and let it rest on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	 Sometimes a fracture of the neck bones occurs, and pain happens when it bends.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	 And similarly in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And if this happens and you want to know whether it will be healed or not, take note if his hands become softened, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, there is no pain felt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is mortal in many ways, and if the hands are silent and feel well when they are pulled or pricked, know that the bone joint is saved, and that the patient should be cured if care is taken.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	 If something similar happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take care if the pain is from soft parts, and if there are accidents that are in hands, and the back gives a jump with involuntary movement;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And when it has been laid on its stomach, it jumps with involuntary movement.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And if it is prodded on the back and it wants to heal, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	 Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Do not labor at all in his treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen to him, it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	 And the treatment is that you reward him if there is an abscess heated, then place on it spine oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	 Then place one of the comforting and drying ointments on it and tie it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And he must not sleep on that part where he feels pain until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	 If any bone is dislocated, it should be covered with vinegar.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	 Break the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound if it is large with stitches, then treat it with healing ointment until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	 And if the joint of the bone (shoulder) is broken, which is called the "joint of the cow," push your left hand's thumb against it and align it with the other hand within your power, then place the splint and the steel on top if needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Then bind it (the broken joint), and if there is bone protruding, push it back into place, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	 It rarely happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it does happen, there will be only a slight reduction in the size of the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	 Make it long and bend it toward the inside, bringing pain to the patient at the place that is broken and causing it to swell.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	 And the resetting is such that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	 and know which is the fracture and the shape of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	 and if the fracture is only at the neck, then equalize that fracture so that it has its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or declines within, then make the patient lie on his belly, so that the restoration of the break is presented to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	 And when you have made it equal, place the splint on it, then place a stick or rod on top of the splint and hold the fracture so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	 and apply the lever underneath the ribs, as long as the handles are equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	 And if an abscess opens up, do not touch it until the abscess has subsided, and place on it what we have previously said.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	 Then return to restoration, and hold it as needed, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	 And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	 The shoulder blade is what is between the ribs and the neck of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	 The first way is that you take a splint made of coarse material in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	 And tie the heads together with cords, and lift them up and place the patient on top of it.
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	 Then throw the broken arm over the splint, until it comes to rest, and have a bend in the splint in the middle, then lift it up with some heavy thing or the assistant stretches it downwards.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	 Then place the mirrors in equal position to each other, at hand level, until the breaker returns as required.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that one restrains the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two servants that one holds the one who is above the fracture with his hands, and the other holds below along all the limb, and extends each one to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 If you see that the extraction is too strong, hold the ligament under the break, and above the break, and extend each of the attendants to their own part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	 And if the breaker is near the head of the shoulder, then you must place the middle lien under the neck and the other one towards the cost side, beneath the breaker.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	 And in the same manner if the breaker is towards the cost side, then you must place the lien slightly but without effort, so that the breaker is equal on top of the level and on the cost side.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 Then you must equalize the breaker as required and hold it in place if no abscesses come up.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	 And if abscesses come up, do not hold it in place for more than 7 days, and put soft linen soaked in rose oil on top of them until the abscesses are calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	 Then hold, and the method of holding is that you place the elbow on the dislocation, then bring the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And cover it, and hold above the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	 And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint than the others on the dislocation, and have two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the dislocation three fingers of each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 Then tighten (or compress) on the studs (possibly referring to a splint), as I said at the beginning of the chapter concerning fractures, more firmly and less when loosening.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	 And if you see the position of the studs (possibly referring to a splint) and the tightening, as we have said, when restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Then observe every three hours the healing (or the suture), that no inflammation arises there or pus comes to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	 And if no such accidents occur, do not loosen (or remove) the sutures before three days or more. Let the patient lie on his back and have his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	 And place a bandage of evenly-cut linen underneath the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the fractured limb does not move, or the tendons are not softened.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	 If the direction is by the virtue of medicine, and they are given meat as we have previously mentioned, in such a manner that the meat is first finely minced.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And when it begins to heal, if it becomes thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	 It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be healed within forty days of all this.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And then it must be dislocated and warm baths and herbal treatments should be administered to direct its position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is deformed and blocked, it will take days or two months to dissolve.
de la brisure du bras	In case of a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "forearm," one of which is small and this is the one that follows the elbow.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	 And the others are large, and he who is beneath, turns towards the small hole.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 Sometimes only the large bones break, or sometimes both the large and small ones, and sometimes it happens together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	 When the small bones are broken, the repair and healing are easy.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 And when the large bones are broken, the healing is bad, and they grieve more than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small boil that has been broken, one should extend it slightly and make it level.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	 And if it is a large fracture, then it must be set harder;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	 and extend it towards the keyhole, and press down on the handle of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, and the keyhole in front of him higher, so that the patient does not feel any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 Then extend your arms to the part below yours (the patient's), or one attendant should be on one side and another above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then the mirror adjusts it to its equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the break is in several places, put each one back in its place, and if there is any displacement that pricks the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	 And if there is an open wound with the fracture, I have discussed it in a specific chapter.
si pren la cure.	 Take care (of the patient).
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	 And if at the beginning of the reset there are abscesses that burst, anoint the linen cloth made of rose oil and white beeswax, neither too hard nor too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 Place (the cloth) on top gently until the burst abscess is soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	 Then remove the beeswax, apply the plaster of flour from the mill with plenty of egg, then place the sticks (splints), and the splint of the fracture should be further out and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	 And know that it must have six splints or more depending on different positions.
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	 Whether the fracture is in one bone, or two.
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	 And hold it more above the break than elsewhere, and all day less in loosening, as I said at the beginning of the chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	 The bandages that are above the break should be soft and moist, not hard nor rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And let the thread, with which it is held, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And hold the limb and the joint afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	 If any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must irrigate the limb with hot water until the itching is eased.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 Let the limb not rest narrowly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the binding again, and if the joints are weakened and the bones dislocated, or something similar, advise accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the urine cannot reach the member because it is too narrow, you must soften it with a little medicine, and leave it like that for some days, until the urine flows into it, and then hold it closed.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of the things that we have said come to the patient, do not undo (the binding) until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	 Or, around it then, after that you bind its neck with your hands, and let its neck be even, and guard against movement and turning, and sleep on its back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And know that this break is restored within 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and in us at the fingers, there are few breaks, but it only occurs multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	 And when the plant (or joint) of the hand is broken or bent, the patient must lie crosswise, and sit straight before him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	 Then place his hand on the extended cloth, and the attendant extends the broken bones and makes them equal, placing them correctly until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	 And apply the plaster and poultice, if an abscess does not come, then place a splint according to the size of the limb.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	 And if the fracture is at the front, around the navel of the thigh, make a bandage of cloths and instruct the patient to bind it on their broken thigh.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 Then bind a long strip of cloth and make it as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside [of the bone], then you must place a splint above and another below in the sole, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it completely around the hand, and compress the ligament between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	 And if the fracture comes to any of the fingers, whether it is the back or the front, set it straight, as necessary.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	 And bind with the palm and if you see one that is crooked, place a small straight splint to lift the fracture and do not allow it to move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	 And if the fracture is in any other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, set it straight and bind it to the healthy finger that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	 Or tie them all together tightly, as is appropriate, or place a splint upon it, as one would a pouch.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 and take care in the restoration and arrangement of an abscess, and treat those who come for it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is well seen when it twists forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 And the restoration is that one ties the ligament above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	 The patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his ligament equally on his side.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And this is when the break has entered the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, it is one of the ligaments toward the knee, and the other ligaments below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	 If it is near the knee, then the ligaments should be loosened at the knee, and the extension should be below.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 Then put the mirrors the bone equal to its two hands, as it should be according to its natural shape, and then place the splint, and the ligature, if an abscess does not come up.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	 And if there is an abscess burning, let it be appeased first, then return to your work and to your care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 The ligature is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	 It is necessary that you wrap above the break and bind it firmly with one or two layers, and remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and push the long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread up.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	 Then turn towards the leg and the calf, then bind with bands, then place on the fracture splints, and place a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	 Use a bandage of soft cloth measuring about 12 fingers between the leg and the calf to equalize the bindings, then start binding in the form of 3 or 4 turns on the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	 and as you go higher up the splint, loosen the bindings.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	 Then insert the threads between the leg and calf that you had placed earlier, bind three splints above them, then go back below the top thread to the foot end until you reach the heel.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 Keep it immobile in its place, then leave it like that, so that no abscess or inflammation or any similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	 And if it happens, dislocate [the bone], and align that which comes out, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	 If there are broken bones protruding, it is necessary to set them, if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	 And if one cannot, then it is necessary to break the bone and draw out marrow.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And heal as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	 Sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that splints are set on it, as in the shoulder or arm.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 However, in this kind of restoration, the patient does not necessarily recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thigh is restored within one day, or a little more or less, according to the various complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the road of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint there occurs little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not so much a fracture as a fissure or a wound that causes pain everywhere and feels painful.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	 The restoration is such that one equalizes what is rounded to its sides until it is assembled and moves as much as possible.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	 Then place the arm-brace, and if needed put a round staff there, and hold it as required, then check all the placements that we have mentioned in other breaks, like an abscess or something similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Keep applying to each case whatever is needed, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one is called correctly "badger," and the other is called "fox.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.
